The Verification Agent is the first trust gate in the runtime.
Its job is not just to parse or validate syntax. It must independently evaluate whether the semantic result is acceptable.
Its flow is:
                                                   1. receive result bundle
                                                   2. independently inspect task, target, and evidence
                                                   3. optionally regenerate claim interpretation
                                                   4. compare its findings to the candidate result
                                                   5. produce:
                                                   * VRF
                                                   * optional CNF
                                                   * optional dispute/conflict metadata
Example:
VRF{target:c.correlation.001 status:verified method:consensus}
If the Verification Agent disagrees, the claim may be marked:
                                                   * pending
                                                   * disputed
                                                   * rejected
This keeps memory from becoming polluted by untrusted outputs.
________________


14. Memory Agent Behavior
The Memory Agent makes Atrahasis cumulative.
Its responsibilities are:
                                                   * query semantic memory before new work begins
                                                   * retrieve reusable objects and bundles
                                                   * detect canonical duplicates
                                                   * write admitted bundles into storage
                                                   * mark supersession or reuse links
                                                   * expose existing knowledge to agents
When a verified claim arrives, the Memory Agent determines:
                                                   * is this new
                                                   * is this equivalent to existing knowledge
                                                   * does this supersede prior knowledge
                                                   * should this be stored in canonical tier or trusted tier
This turns one-off computation into reusable semantic intelligence.
________________


15. Shared Semantic Memory Structure
The shared semantic memory in the first runtime should store semantic bundles, not isolated loose objects only.
A stored bundle should usually contain:
                                                   * task context
                                                   * action object(s)
                                                   * claim object(s)
                                                   * evidence object(s)
                                                   * confidence object(s)
                                                   * provenance object(s)
                                                   * verification object(s)
                                                   * canonical hash
                                                   * document and bundle metadata
This allows future retrieval to be rich and reusable.
For example, if a future agent asks for the claim, it can also retrieve:
                                                   * why the claim exists
                                                   * what evidence supported it
                                                   * whether it was verified
                                                   * where it came from
________________


16. Runtime Storage Tiers
Even in the first runtime, storage should support tiers.
Draft Tier
For:
                                                   * intermediate agent outputs
                                                   * partially analyzed semantic bundles
                                                   * unverified candidate objects
Canonical Tier
For:
                                                   * validated and canonicalized semantic artifacts
                                                   * reusable but not fully trusted artifacts if policy allows
Verified Tier
For:
                                                   * semantically canonical
                                                   * successfully verified
                                                   * trusted knowledge objects
This keeps semantic hygiene intact from the beginning.
________________


17. Internal Message Format
Inside the runtime, agent-to-agent communication should already use the AASL-based AACP framing model.
Each message should have:
                                                   * AACP header
                                                   * AASL payload
Example:
HEADER{
 message_id:msg.001
 sender_id:ag.coordination.01
 receiver_id:ag.analysis.01
 message_class:task_request
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
}


PAYLOAD{
 TSK{id:t.climate.001 op:analyze target:ds.climate.44}
}
This is important because it proves that AASL is not only storage format, but operational protocol content.
________________


18. First Query Capabilities
The first runtime should expose only the most important semantic queries initially, but they must be real.
Core query functions should include:
                                                   * get object by ID
                                                   * get all claims for target
                                                   * get all verification records for claim
                                                   * get all evidence linked to claim
                                                   * get all stored bundles for task target
                                                   * get canonical duplicate by hash
                                                   * get latest verified result for semantic target
These are enough to prove semantic reuse and verification-aware retrieval.
________________


19. First Persistence Model
The first runtime persistence model should be simple but principled.
It should persist:
                                                   * .aas artifact form for document durability
                                                   * normalized object store for runtime rehydration
                                                   * indexes for:
                                                   * object ID
                                                   * type
                                                   * target
                                                   * verification status
                                                   * canonical hash
This gives the runtime:
                                                   * file durability
                                                   * semantic queryability
                                                   * memory reuse
without waiting for a much larger distributed store.
________________


20. Runtime Validation Points
Validation should occur at four points in the first runtime:
                                                   1. after compilation into AASL
                                                   2. before agent result acceptance
                                                   3. before verification comparison
                                                   4. before memory admission
This ensures semantic quality at every meaningful transition.
The runtime should never allow:
                                                   * malformed semantic objects
                                                   * invalid ontology values
                                                   * broken references
                                                   * noncanonical artifacts into trusted memory
________________


21. Canonicalization Points
Canonicalization should occur at least twice:
                                                   1. after compiler output
                                                   2. before final storage and hashing
Why twice:
                                                   * first to normalize ingress
                                                   * second to normalize any agent-generated or agent-enriched artifacts before memory commit
This ensures the storage and verification layers work from stable semantic form.
________________


22. First Verification Policy
The first runtime should use a very explicit and simple verification policy.
For example:
A candidate semantic result enters verified tier only if:
                                                   * structurally valid
                                                   * canonically valid
                                                   * references resolved
                                                   * verification agent agrees with result
                                                   * target hash matches canonical target state
                                                   * no active dispute exists
This creates a strong trust boundary even in the first system.
________________


23. Observability in the First Runtime
The first runtime should include basic observability from day one.
At minimum it should track:
                                                   * number of tasks received
                                                   * number of tasks reused from memory
                                                   * number of new claims generated
                                                   * number of verified claims
                                                   * number of rejected/disputed claims
                                                   * number of stored semantic bundles
                                                   * average agent task latency
                                                   * average verification latency
This proves whether the semantic loop is actually creating reusable value.
________________


24. Human Inspection Layer
Even in the first runtime, there should be a minimal inspection interface.
This can be simple, but it should let a developer inspect:
                                                   * the active runtime objects
                                                   * the current task graph
                                                   * the last verified bundle
                                                   * stored semantic bundles for a target
                                                   * disputes and rejected outputs
This makes it possible to debug the first full semantic loop end-to-end.
________________


25. Failure Handling
The first runtime must define failure states clearly.
Possible failure cases:
                                                   * compile failure
                                                   * parse failure
                                                   * validation failure
                                                   * runtime resolution failure
                                                   * agent execution failure
                                                   * verification failure
                                                   * storage admission failure
Each failure should result in:
                                                   * explicit state transition
                                                   * diagnostic emission
                                                   * optional quarantine bundle
                                                   * no silent trust promotion
This is essential for keeping the system trustworthy during early implementation.
________________


26. First Runtime API Surface
The first runtime should expose a small but complete API surface.
Essential operations:
                                                   * submit input
                                                   * compile to AASL
                                                   * create task
                                                   * execute task
                                                   * retrieve semantic result
                                                   * retrieve verification status
                                                   * query memory
                                                   * inspect stored bundle
                                                   * export bundle to .aas
This is enough to prove the operational loop and support tooling.
________________


27. Minimal But Complete Storage Schema
The first runtime store should include at least these conceptual tables/collections:
                                                   * documents
                                                   * objects
                                                   * references
                                                   * bundles
                                                   * verification records
                                                   * provenance records
                                                   * canonical hashes
                                                   * task executions
This is sufficient to:
                                                   * load semantic bundles
                                                   * query them
                                                   * rehydrate runtime state
                                                   * reuse prior knowledge
________________


28. First Runtime Success Criteria
The first runtime is successful only if it proves all of the following:
                                                   1. A user can submit non-AASL input.
                                                   2. The system can compile it into AASL.
                                                   3. The coordinator can assign an AASL task.
                                                   4. Agents can return AASL objects.
                                                   5. The verification agent can validate semantic results.
                                                   6. Verified semantic bundles can be stored.
                                                   7. A second equivalent task can retrieve and reuse stored knowledge instead of recomputing it.
That last point is especially important. It proves Atrahasis is becoming cumulative intelligence rather than a stateless agent loop.
________________


29. What This Runtime Proves
If built correctly, this first runtime proves:
                                                   * AASL can function as the internal language of Atrahasis
                                                   * AASL-based AACP can coordinate agents
                                                   * semantic verification is tractable
                                                   * shared semantic memory can reduce repeated work
                                                   * the language, runtime, compiler, validator, and storage layers actually compose into one working system
This is the first real end-to-end proof of the entire architectural thesis.
________________


30. Final Summary
The first minimal working Atrahasis runtime built entirely around AASL is a complete semantic operating loop composed of:
                                                   * AASC ingress compilation
                                                   * AASL task objects
                                                   * coordinator-driven orchestration
                                                   * research and analysis agents operating on AASL
                                                   * verification agent producing VRF trust objects
                                                   * memory agent managing semantic cache and storage
                                                   * shared semantic memory with canonical and verified tiers
                                                   * AASL-based internal messaging
                                                   * runtime querying and result reuse
It is the smallest complete system that proves Atrahasis can operate as an AASL-native intelligence environment rather than a collection of loosely connected tools.
________________


The next thing we should work on is:
The full repo architecture and implementation breakdown for this first AASL-native Atrahasis runtime
That means defining:
                                                   * services
                                                   * modules
                                                   * package boundaries
                                                   * APIs
                                                   * storage schema
                                                   * runtime processes
                                                   * agent contracts
                                                   * message contracts
                                                   * directory/repo structure
That is the correct next step because now the architecture is complete enough to translate directly into implementation.
Full Repo Architecture and Implementation Breakdown for the First AASL-Native Atrahasis Runtime
This is the first concrete implementation architecture for the initial working Atrahasis runtime built entirely around AASL. The goal here is no longer just conceptual alignment. The goal is to define a repo and service structure that can actually be built, tested, extended, and eventually scaled into the broader Atrahasis system.
This architecture must satisfy the full loop already defined:
                                                   * external input enters
                                                   * AASC compiles it into AASL
                                                   * parser and validator admit it
                                                   * coordinator turns it into task flow
                                                   * agents operate on AASL
                                                   * verification evaluates results
                                                   * memory stores verified semantic bundles
                                                   * future tasks reuse that knowledge
So the repo architecture must reflect the actual semantic runtime, not a generic microservice template.
________________


1. Top-Level Architectural Principle
The first runtime should be built as a modular monorepo with service boundaries, not as one giant application and not yet as dozens of independently deployed distributed services.
That means:
                                                   * one repo
                                                   * multiple packages/modules
                                                   * a few runtime services/processes
                                                   * shared contracts and libraries
                                                   * clear upgrade path to later distributed separation
This is the right shape because it gives:
                                                   * implementation speed
                                                   * architectural rigor
                                                   * code reuse
                                                   * one source of truth for AASL contracts
                                                   * easier testing and debugging
                                                   * future extraction path into separate deployable services
________________


2. Recommended Top-Level Repo Structure
A good first repo structure should look like this:
atrahasis-runtime/
├── apps/
├── services/
├── packages/
├── schemas/
├── testdata/
├── tests/
├── tools/
├── docs/
├── infra/
└── scripts/
Each top-level area has a distinct role.
________________


3. apps/ — Human and Operator Entry Points
This folder contains executable application entry points.
Recommended initial apps:
apps/
├── api-gateway/
├── operator-console/
├── aasl-cli/
└── runtime-dev-shell/
3.1 api-gateway/
The external ingress layer.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * receive user/API input
                                                   * route to AASC ingress pipeline
                                                   * expose task submission endpoints
                                                   * expose retrieval endpoints
                                                   * expose bundle export endpoints
3.2 operator-console/
Internal inspection UI for:
                                                   * task execution
                                                   * stored bundles
                                                   * verification status
                                                   * disputes
                                                   * runtime health
3.3 aasl-cli/
Developer/operator CLI for:
                                                   * compile
                                                   * validate
                                                   * inspect
                                                   * query
                                                   * export
                                                   * replay task flows
3.4 runtime-dev-shell/
A local development/debug app for:
                                                   * loading test AASL
                                                   * running agents manually
                                                   * simulating full runtime cycles
________________


4. services/ — Runtime Processes
These are the major live processes in the first runtime.
Recommended initial services:
services/
├── ingress-service/
├── coordinator-service/
├── agent-service/
├── verification-service/
├── memory-service/
├── query-service/
└── storage-service/
These can initially run as distinct modules/processes in one deployment environment.
________________


5. services/ingress-service/
This is the system boundary where external content becomes AASL.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * accept raw input
                                                   * classify source type
                                                   * invoke AASC
                                                   * produce validated task bundles
                                                   * hand tasks to coordinator
Internal submodules:
services/ingress-service/
├── src/
│   ├── controllers/
│   ├── adapters/
│   ├── compile-pipeline/
│   ├── validators/
│   └── handoff/
Key interfaces:
                                                   * submit task
                                                   * submit document
                                                   * compile-only
                                                   * preview canonical AASL
________________


6. services/coordinator-service/
This is the orchestration brain of the first runtime.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * receive semantic task bundles
                                                   * check memory-first execution
                                                   * dispatch work to agents
                                                   * collect outputs
                                                   * send for verification
                                                   * finalize task state
Internal submodules:
services/coordinator-service/
├── src/
│   ├── task-router/
│   ├── workflow-engine/
│   ├── assignment-engine/
│   ├── bundle-collector/
│   └── state-machine/
This service should own the task lifecycle.
________________


7. services/agent-service/
This is the host for the first agent roles.
Instead of separate process per agent type at first, use one service hosting multiple agent role implementations.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * run research agent
                                                   * run analysis agent
                                                   * run memory-support calls if needed
                                                   * execute semantic tasks
                                                   * emit AASL result bundles
Recommended structure:
services/agent-service/
├── src/
│   ├── agents/
│   │   ├── coordinator-support/
│   │   ├── research-agent/
│   │   ├── analysis-agent/
│   │   ├── verification-prep/
│   │   └── memory-agent-client/
│   ├── model-interfaces/
│   ├── execution/
│   └── outputs/
The agent roles are runtime behaviors implemented against shared AASL contracts.
________________


8. services/verification-service/
This service evaluates result bundles.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * receive candidate result bundles
                                                   * independently inspect target/evidence/claim structure
                                                   * compare expected semantics
                                                   * produce VRF objects
                                                   * emit disputes or approvals
Structure:
services/verification-service/
├── src/
│   ├── evaluators/
│   ├── comparison/
│   ├── verification-policy/
│   ├── dispute-handler/
│   └── outputs/
This should remain strict and policy-driven.
________________


9. services/memory-service/
This service makes the runtime cumulative.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * memory-first lookup
                                                   * bundle retrieval
                                                   * duplicate detection
                                                   * canonical hash lookup
                                                   * store admission orchestration
                                                   * semantic reuse logic
Structure:
services/memory-service/
├── src/
│   ├── lookup/
│   ├── bundle-store/
│   ├── dedup/
│   ├── admission/
│   └── tier-manager/
This service is the interface to shared semantic memory.
________________


10. services/query-service/
This service exposes semantic retrieval.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * object lookup
                                                   * claim lookup
                                                   * bundle retrieval
                                                   * graph traversal
                                                   * document-scoped queries
                                                   * verified-tier-only queries
Structure:
services/query-service/
├── src/
│   ├── lookup/
│   ├── traversal/
│   ├── filters/
│   ├── result-shaping/
│   └── query-api/
This service should sit on top of storage and runtime abstractions.
________________


11. services/storage-service/
This service manages persistence.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * document persistence
                                                   * object persistence
                                                   * reference persistence
                                                   * version state
                                                   * index maintenance
                                                   * rehydration support
Structure:
services/storage-service/
├── src/
│   ├── document-store/
│   ├── object-store/
│   ├── reference-store/
│   ├── index-store/
│   ├── versioning/
│   └── rehydration/
This service must be transaction-aware.
________________


12. packages/ — Shared Internal Libraries
This is the most important folder in the monorepo. It should contain reusable libraries shared by all services.
Recommended structure:
packages/
├── aasl-core/
├── aasl-parser/
├── aasl-runtime/
├── aasl-validator/
├── aasl-canonicalizer/
├── aasl-compiler/
├── aasl-query/
├── aasl-storage-contracts/
├── aasl-security/
├── aacp-contracts/
├── agent-contracts/
├── shared-types/
└── observability/

________________
13. packages/aasl-core/
This contains the fundamental shared language model.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * object type definitions
                                                   * section definitions
                                                   * core enums
                                                   * version constants
                                                   * shared identifiers
                                                   * semantic metadata types
This package must be dependency-light and act as the base for the whole system.
________________


14. packages/aasl-parser/
Implements the parser architecture already defined.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * lexer
                                                   * grammar parser
                                                   * CST
                                                   * AST
                                                   * symbol table
                                                   * diagnostics
                                                   * parse modes
Exports:
                                                   * parse APIs
                                                   * parse result types
                                                   * diagnostics model
Every other subsystem depends on this package.
________________


15. packages/aasl-runtime/
Implements the runtime object model.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * runtime object store
                                                   * reference resolver
                                                   * state tracking
                                                   * hydration
                                                   * mutation primitives
                                                   * object lifecycle handling
This is the semantic in-memory substrate used by services.
________________


16. packages/aasl-validator/
Implements validation.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * structural rules
                                                   * template rules
                                                   * type/value rules
                                                   * ontology rules
                                                   * reference rules
                                                   * canonical rules
                                                   * document rules
                                                   * validation reports
This package should expose strict and tolerant modes.
________________


17. packages/aasl-canonicalizer/
Implements canonical normalization.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * operator normalization
                                                   * field ordering
                                                   * ID normalization
                                                   * batch ordering
                                                   * timestamp normalization
                                                   * null omission
                                                   * canonical emission prep
This package is central for:
                                                   * hashing
                                                   * deduplication
                                                   * stable storage
                                                   * verification
________________


18. packages/aasl-compiler/
Implements AASC core.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * source adapters
                                                   * semantic extraction interfaces
                                                   * ontology mapping
                                                   * ID assignment
                                                   * canonical output generation
                                                   * reverse rendering
Subpackages/modules should include:
                                                   * text adapter
                                                   * markdown adapter
                                                   * JSON adapter
                                                   * draft AASL normalizer
________________


19. packages/aasl-query/
Implements semantic querying.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * ID lookup
                                                   * type lookup
                                                   * filter engine
                                                   * traversal engine
                                                   * bundle result shaping
                                                   * state-aware query helpers
This package should support both runtime-backed and storage-backed retrieval.
________________


20. packages/aasl-storage-contracts/
Defines the abstraction layer between semantic systems and persistence.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * document persistence interfaces
                                                   * object persistence interfaces
                                                   * bundle persistence interfaces
                                                   * rehydration contracts
                                                   * versioning contracts
                                                   * admission result contracts
This allows the storage engine to evolve without rewriting semantic systems.
________________


21. packages/aasl-security/
Implements integrity and security primitives.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * checksum generation
                                                   * canonical hash generation
                                                   * artifact signing interfaces
                                                   * verification metadata contracts
                                                   * replay metadata handling
                                                   * trust metadata types
Even if signatures are basic at first, the contract surface should be defined here.
________________


22. packages/aacp-contracts/
Defines the AASL-based AACP message structure.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * header types
                                                   * message classes
                                                   * payload contracts
                                                   * message validation helpers
                                                   * correlation/thread/workflow IDs
This package ensures all services speak the same message language.
________________


23. packages/agent-contracts/
Defines the semantic contracts for agents.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * agent role interfaces
                                                   * input bundle types
                                                   * output bundle types
                                                   * execution result contracts
                                                   * verification result contracts
                                                   * agent capability declarations
This ensures agents are replaceable without changing the orchestration model.
________________


24. packages/shared-types/
Holds general shared infrastructure types.
Examples:
                                                   * pagination structures
                                                   * time wrappers
                                                   * error objects
                                                   * diagnostic envelopes
                                                   * job status structures
Keep this generic and free of AASL-specific semantics when possible.
________________


25. packages/observability/
Shared logging, metrics, tracing, and event instrumentation.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * task lifecycle metrics
                                                   * compile metrics
                                                   * validation counts
                                                   * query latency
                                                   * verification outcomes
                                                   * storage admission stats
This package should be used by all services.
________________


26. schemas/ — Formal Contracts
This folder stores formal schema documents, not implementation code.
Recommended contents:
schemas/
├── aasl/
├── aacp/
├── agents/

└── api/
Examples:
                                                   * canonical object templates

                                                   * API schemas
                                                   * validation rule manifests
                                                   * storage entity definitions
This folder becomes the formal contract layer for cross-service rigor.

31. infra/ — Deployment and Environment Definitions

infra/
