└── observability/
For the first runtime, Docker Compose is enough, but structure it so it can later move to Kubernetes.
Initial infra should cover:
                                                   * API gateway
                                                   * coordinator
                                                   * agent service
                                                   * verification service
                                                   * memory service
                                                   * storage backend
                                                   * optional query service
                                                   * optional operator console
________________


32. scripts/ — Operational Scripts
Useful bootstrap commands:
                                                   * start local runtime
                                                   * seed ontology registry
                                                   * load test fixtures
                                                   * run full end-to-end scenario
                                                   * rebuild indexes
                                                   * export knowledge bundle
                                                   * run verification replay test
This helps engineers run the whole system consistently.
________________


33. Runtime Process Model
For the first working runtime, the process model should be:
api-gateway
coordinator-service
agent-service
verification-service
memory-service
storage-service
query-service
These services can initially communicate over:
                                                   * internal HTTP/gRPC
                                                   * or queue-backed async messaging where needed
But all payload semantics should use AACP + AASL contracts.
________________


34. Recommended Storage Backend Shape
Even without locking into a final DB choice, the repo should separate persistence concerns into:
                                                   * document persistence
                                                   * object persistence
                                                   * reference persistence
                                                   * index persistence
                                                   * bundle persistence
A practical first implementation could use:
                                                   * relational DB for normalized object/reference metadata
                                                   * object/blob store for canonical .aas artifacts
                                                   * in-memory cache for hot runtime/query access
But keep this behind aasl-storage-contracts.
________________


35. First Core APIs
The first runtime should expose these API groups.
Ingress API
                                                   * submit input
                                                   * compile preview
                                                   * submit task
Task API
                                                   * get task status
                                                   * get task bundle
                                                   * get execution trace
Query API
                                                   * get object by ID
                                                   * get claim bundle
                                                   * search by target/type/status
Memory API
                                                   * retrieve reusable bundle
                                                   * inspect canonical hash
                                                   * inspect verification status
Export API
                                                   * export .aas
                                                   * export JSON
                                                   * export semantic bundle
These APIs should be implemented in the gateway/query/memory services.
________________


36. First Internal Message Contracts
Core AACP message classes needed immediately:
                                                   * task_request
                                                   * task_result
                                                   * verification_request
                                                   * verification_result
                                                   * knowledge_update
                                                   * error_report
                                                   * state_update
These should live in packages/aacp-contracts and be used everywhere.
________________


37. First Bundle Contract
The runtime should standardize on a semantic bundle contract.
A bundle should include:
                                                   * bundle ID
                                                   * task context
                                                   * participating objects
                                                   * source document refs if any
                                                   * validation state
                                                   * canonical state
                                                   * verification state
                                                   * canonical hash
                                                   * provenance metadata
                                                   * storage tier target
This is the unit that moves through the runtime more often than raw individual objects.
________________


38. First Service Dependency Rules
To prevent chaos, define dependency boundaries early.
Recommended rules:
                                                   * apps may depend on packages, not on service internals
                                                   * services may depend on packages and storage contracts
                                                   * packages should not depend on apps
                                                   * core packages should not depend on service implementations
                                                   * aasl-core should be lowest-level
                                                   * aasl-parser, validator, canonicalizer, runtime depend on aasl-core
                                                   * service orchestration depends on all needed packages, not vice versa
This keeps the codebase sane as it grows.
________________


39. First End-to-End Scenario in the Repo
The repo should ship with one canonical demo flow.
Example scenario:
                                                   1. submit climate analysis prompt
                                                   2. compile into AASL task
                                                   3. coordinator dispatches to research + analysis
                                                   4. candidate claim bundle returned
                                                   5. verification evaluates bundle
                                                   6. verified bundle stored
                                                   7. second equivalent request hits memory and returns reused result
This scenario should be runnable from scripts/ and testable in CI.
That single scenario proves the architecture.
________________


40. Final Summary
The first AASL-native Atrahasis runtime should be built as a modular monorepo with:
                                                   * apps/ for user/operator entry points
                                                   * services/ for live runtime processes
                                                   * packages/ for shared semantic libraries
                                                   * schemas/ for formal contracts
                                                   * testdata/ and tests/ for conformance and end-to-end proof
                                                   * tools/, docs/, infra/, and scripts/ for operability
Its first service set should include:
                                                   * ingress
                                                   * coordinator
                                                   * agent execution
                                                   * verification
                                                   * memory
                                                   * query
                                                   * storage
Its core shared packages should include:
                                                   * parser
                                                   * runtime
                                                   * validator
                                                   * canonicalizer
                                                   * compiler
                                                   * query
                                                   * security
                                                   * AACP contracts
                                                   * agent contracts
That repo shape is the first implementation-ready form of the entire AASL-native Atrahasis runtime.
________________


The next thing we should work on is:
The exact agent contracts and lifecycle definitions for the first five agents
That means defining, for each agent:
                                                   * inputs
                                                   * outputs
                                                   * allowed actions
                                                   * state transitions
                                                   * failure states
                                                   * memory interactions
                                                   * verification expectations
That is the cleanest next step because the repo structure is now defined, and the next most important implementation unit is the actual behavior contract for each runtime agent.
Exact Agent Contracts and Lifecycle Definitions for the First Five Agents
With the repo architecture defined, the next implementation-critical layer is the behavior contract for each agent. These contracts make the runtime executable because they define exactly what each agent may receive, what it may produce, how it moves through state, how it interacts with memory, and how failure or verification are handled.
The first runtime uses five agents:
                                                   * Coordinator Agent
                                                   * Research Agent
                                                   * Analysis Agent
                                                   * Verification Agent
                                                   * Memory Agent
These are not just role names. Each one needs a precise operational contract.
________________


1. Common Agent Contract Model
Before defining each agent individually, the runtime should establish a shared base contract that all agents inherit.
Every agent should have:
                                                   * agent_id
                                                   * role
                                                   * capabilities
                                                   * supported_task_ops
                                                   * input_bundle_schema
                                                   * output_bundle_schema
                                                   * state_model
                                                   * failure_model
                                                   * memory_access_scope
                                                   * verification_requirements
Every agent should interact through the AACP + AASL message model, not through ad hoc method calls or raw text.
So the universal agent flow is:
receive AACP message
    ↓
hydrate AASL payload into runtime objects
    ↓
validate admissibility for this agent role
    ↓
execute agent role logic
    ↓
emit AASL result bundle
    ↓
return through AACP

________________
2. Universal Agent Lifecycle
All first-generation agents should share a common lifecycle.
2.1 Registered
The agent is known to the runtime and available for assignment.
2.2 Idle
The agent is alive but not currently processing a task.
2.3 Assigned
A task bundle has been routed to the agent.
2.4 Hydrating
The agent is loading runtime objects, references, and memory context.
2.5 Executing
The agent is performing its role-specific work.
2.6 Emitting
The agent is packaging output into a semantic bundle.
2.7 Completed
The agent successfully returned a valid result.
2.8 Failed
The agent encountered an unrecoverable execution failure.
2.9 Rejected
The agent refused or could not accept the bundle due to contract mismatch, validation, or policy rules.
That common lifecycle should be modeled consistently across all agents.
________________


3. Universal Agent Input Contract
Every agent should receive a task bundle, not a naked object.
A first-runtime bundle should contain:
                                                   * bundle_id
                                                   * task_id
                                                   * workflow_id
                                                   * conversation_id
                                                   * message_id
                                                   * origin_agent_id
                                                   * target_agent_id
                                                   * primary_task (TSK)
                                                   * supporting_objects
                                                   * relevant_constraints
                                                   * memory_context
                                                   * document_context
                                                   * validation_state
                                                   * canonical_state
The agent contract should require that the bundle already be:
                                                   * structurally parsed
                                                   * runtime-hydrated enough for consumption
                                                   * minimally validated for delivery
Agents should not be expected to accept arbitrary malformed bundles.
________________


4. Universal Agent Output Contract
Every agent should return a result bundle.
At minimum it should contain:
                                                   * bundle_id
                                                   * source_task_id
                                                   * produced_by
                                                   * execution_status
                                                   * produced_objects
                                                   * diagnostics
                                                   * provenance_append
                                                   * next_recommended_action
                                                   * optional error_objects
This keeps all agent outputs uniform.
________________


5. Universal Failure Model
Each agent should be able to fail in predictable categories.
5.1 Input Rejection
The task bundle was not admissible for this role.
5.2 Resolution Failure
Required references or memory context could not be resolved.
5.3 Execution Failure
The agent’s internal reasoning or processing failed.
5.4 Policy Failure
The requested task violated role, ontology, or runtime policy.
5.5 Emission Failure
The agent produced output that failed internal validation or could not be serialized into AASL.
5.6 Timeout / Resource Failure
The agent exceeded runtime limits.
Each failure should return:
                                                   * failure category
                                                   * semantic error object or structured diagnostics
                                                   * task correlation identifiers
                                                   * whether retry is allowed
________________


6. Coordinator Agent Contract
The Coordinator Agent is the orchestration authority for the first runtime.
6.1 Purpose
The Coordinator controls the semantic task lifecycle from admission through storage decision.
6.2 Allowed Inputs
The Coordinator may receive:
                                                   * newly compiled task bundles from ingress
                                                   * follow-up state updates from agents
                                                   * verification results
                                                   * retry or failure reports
Its primary input object is usually:
                                                   * TSK
                                                   * optional CST
                                                   * optional supporting DS, PRV, TIM, or context bundle metadata
6.3 Allowed Outputs
The Coordinator may emit:
                                                   * task_request bundles to Research or Analysis Agents
                                                   * verification_request bundles to Verification Agent
                                                   * knowledge_update bundles to Memory Agent
                                                   * state_update messages to API/operator layers
                                                   * error_report if workflow cannot continue
6.4 Role-Specific Responsibilities
The Coordinator must:
                                                   * accept semantic task bundles
                                                   * inspect task type and constraints
                                                   * request memory-first lookup before computation
                                                   * decide whether reuse is sufficient
                                                   * decompose work when reuse is not sufficient
                                                   * assign work to role-appropriate agents
                                                   * collect partial or final results
                                                   * determine whether verification is required
                                                   * route successful results to memory admission
6.5 Coordinator State Machine
Its task-level lifecycle should be:
received
  → memory_check
  → assignment
  → waiting_for_result
  → verification_pending
  → memory_commit_pending
  → completed
Failure branches:
                                                   * rejected
                                                   * execution_failed
                                                   * verification_failed
                                                   * storage_failed
6.6 Memory Interaction
The Coordinator does not directly perform storage logic, but it must:
                                                   * request lookup from Memory Agent
                                                   * interpret whether returned bundle is reusable
                                                   * attach memory hit/miss status to workflow state
                                                   * route verified results for memory admission
6.7 Verification Expectations
The Coordinator must not mark a claim as trusted or finalized on its own. It must wait for Verification Agent output before requesting trusted storage.
________________


7. Research Agent Contract
The Research Agent is responsible for semantic evidence extraction and source-grounded fact gathering.
7.1 Purpose
The Research Agent transforms source context into structured evidence candidates and preliminary semantic observations.
7.2 Allowed Inputs
The Research Agent may receive:
                                                   * TSK with an operation such as extract, analyze, summarize, or gather
                                                   * referenced DS objects
                                                   * supporting provenance or document context
                                                   * constraints
                                                   * optional pre-existing memory context
A typical task bundle to Research Agent should contain:
                                                   * primary TSK
                                                   * source artifact(s)
                                                   * extraction scope
                                                   * optional target concepts
7.3 Allowed Outputs
The Research Agent may emit:
                                                   * ACT
                                                   * EVD
                                                   * PRV
                                                   * optional draft CLM
                                                   * optional TIM
                                                   * source-location-aware semantic fragments
It should generally avoid producing final authoritative verification conclusions.
7.4 Role-Specific Responsibilities
The Research Agent must:
                                                   * inspect source data or documents
                                                   * extract semantically relevant units
                                                   * identify evidence-bearing structures
                                                   * preserve source traceability
                                                   * emit evidence objects and preliminary findings
                                                   * attach provenance
7.5 Research Agent State Machine
assigned
  → hydrate_sources
  → inspect_sources
  → extract_semantics
  → emit_evidence_bundle
  → completed
Failure branches:
                                                   * source_unavailable
                                                   * unresolved_reference
                                                   * extraction_failed
                                                   * provenance_incomplete
7.6 Memory Interaction
The Research Agent may read from memory for context enrichment, but it should not directly write to memory.
It may request:
                                                   * known dataset identities
                                                   * known entity IDs
                                                   * prior evidence objects
                                                   * known source mappings
7.7 Verification Expectations
Research outputs are usually verification-input artifacts, not verification-final artifacts. They should be suitable for downstream Analysis and Verification Agents.
________________


8. Analysis Agent Contract
The Analysis Agent converts evidence and context into formal semantic claims.
8.1 Purpose
The Analysis Agent is responsible for generating structured conclusions from semantic evidence.
8.2 Allowed Inputs
The Analysis Agent may receive:
                                                   * TSK
                                                   * EVD
                                                   * PRV
                                                   * relevant DS
                                                   * optional draft CLM
                                                   * memory context
                                                   * constraints
It should typically receive already-hydrated evidence bundles, not raw documents as its primary substrate.
8.3 Allowed Outputs
The Analysis Agent may emit:
                                                   * ACT
                                                   * CLM
                                                   * CNF
                                                   * PRV
                                                   * optional TIM
                                                   * optional supporting derived semantic links
This is the main claim-producing agent in the first runtime.
8.4 Role-Specific Responsibilities
The Analysis Agent must:
                                                   * inspect evidence bundles
                                                   * identify semantic relationships
                                                   * classify the relationship using ontology-approved claim types
                                                   * produce formal claims
                                                   * attach confidence
                                                   * preserve traceability back to evidence and source bundles
8.5 Analysis Agent State Machine
assigned
  → hydrate_context
  → inspect_evidence
  → formulate_claims
  → score_confidence
  → emit_claim_bundle
  → completed
Failure branches:
                                                   * insufficient_evidence
                                                   * ambiguous_mapping
                                                   * analysis_failed
                                                   * output_not_admissible
8.6 Memory Interaction
The Analysis Agent may read memory to:
                                                   * reuse known entities
                                                   * compare with prior claims
                                                   * inspect prior canonical bundles
                                                   * avoid redundant ID creation
It should not directly promote new knowledge to memory.
8.7 Verification Expectations
Analysis outputs must be structured for verification. That means claims should include enough semantic support that the Verification Agent can independently evaluate them.
________________


9. Verification Agent Contract
The Verification Agent is the first trust gate for candidate semantic knowledge.
9.1 Purpose
The Verification Agent determines whether candidate semantic results are sufficiently supported and semantically consistent to be promoted toward trusted memory.
9.2 Allowed Inputs
The Verification Agent may receive:
                                                   * source task context
                                                   * result bundle from Analysis or Research flow
                                                   * supporting evidence and provenance
                                                   * relevant constraints
                                                   * optional prior stored equivalent bundle for comparison
Its input should always include the target object(s) to be verified.
9.3 Allowed Outputs
The Verification Agent may emit:
                                                   * VRF
                                                   * optional CNF if verification confidence is explicitly modeled
                                                   * dispute or rejection diagnostics
                                                   * optional comparison metadata
                                                   * optional supersession recommendation
9.4 Role-Specific Responsibilities
The Verification Agent must:
                                                   * independently inspect the target bundle
                                                   * confirm structural and semantic coherence
                                                   * compare claims against evidence and task scope
                                                   * determine verification status
                                                   * emit verification records bound to exact semantic targets
                                                   * avoid overstepping into policy promotion decisions that belong to Memory or Coordinator logic
9.5 Verification Agent State Machine
assigned
  → hydrate_candidate_bundle
  → inspect_target_claims
  → compare_against_evidence
  → determine_status
  → emit_verification_record
  → completed
Possible status results:
                                                   * verified
                                                   * pending
                                                   * disputed
                                                   * rejected
9.6 Memory Interaction
The Verification Agent may read memory to compare:
                                                   * existing canonical hashes
                                                   * prior verification records
                                                   * current accepted versions
                                                   * conflict history
It should not directly write final accepted knowledge to storage. It returns trust state to the Coordinator and Memory layers.
9.7 Verification Expectations
This agent defines whether a result is admissible for higher trust tiers. Its output must be tightly bound to canonical target IDs and semantic state.
________________


10. Memory Agent Contract
The Memory Agent is the semantic continuity layer of the runtime.
10.1 Purpose
The Memory Agent manages semantic reuse, duplicate detection, admission, and retrieval across the shared semantic memory.
10.2 Allowed Inputs
The Memory Agent may receive:
                                                   * lookup requests before task execution
                                                   * candidate bundles after verification
                                                   * object or bundle identity requests
                                                   * deduplication checks
                                                   * storage promotion requests
10.3 Allowed Outputs
The Memory Agent may emit:
                                                   * memory hit bundle
                                                   * memory miss result
                                                   * canonical duplicate result
                                                   * admission decision
                                                   * storage-tier placement decision
                                                   * supersession record recommendation
                                                   * retrieval bundles for agents/coordinator
10.4 Role-Specific Responsibilities
The Memory Agent must:
                                                   * search for reusable semantic knowledge
                                                   * resolve identity reuse where possible
                                                   * detect canonical duplicates
                                                   * determine whether new knowledge is novel or redundant
                                                   * coordinate storage admission into correct tier
                                                   * retrieve semantic bundles for future reuse
10.5 Memory Agent State Machine
Lookup path
assigned
  → inspect_lookup_target
  → query_semantic_memory
  → determine_hit_or_miss
  → emit_lookup_result
  → completed
Admission path
assigned
  → inspect_candidate_bundle
  → check_validation_and_verification_state
  → check_duplicates_and_conflicts
  → assign_storage_tier
  → commit_or_reject
  → emit_admission_result
  → completed
Failure branches:
                                                   * storage_unavailable
                                                   * admission_policy_failed
                                                   * conflict_unresolved
                                                   * canonical_mismatch
10.6 Memory Interaction
This is the one agent whose primary role is memory interaction. It is the gateway between the active runtime and persistent semantic memory.
10.7 Verification Expectations
The Memory Agent should respect verification state but not invent it. It should only promote to high-trust tiers if verification outputs satisfy admission policy.
________________


11. Agent Capability Declarations
Each agent should explicitly declare its supported operations.
Example model:
Coordinator Agent
                                                   * route_task
                                                   * collect_result
                                                   * initiate_verification
                                                   * finalize_workflow
Research Agent
                                                   * extract
                                                   * gather
                                                   * source_inspect
                                                   * evidence_emit
Analysis Agent
                                                   * analyze
                                                   * compare
                                                   * classify
                                                   * claim_emit
Verification Agent
                                                   * verify
                                                   * compare_result
                                                   * dispute
                                                   * verification_emit
Memory Agent
                                                   * lookup
                                                   * deduplicate
                                                   * admit
                                                   * retrieve
                                                   * tier_assign
These capability declarations should live in the agent contracts package and be machine-readable.
________________


12. Allowed Object Production by Role
To prevent semantic sprawl, each agent should be constrained in what it may author directly.
Coordinator Agent may produce
                                                   * workflow/task state metadata
                                                   * routing bundles
                                                   * state updates
                                                   * not primary claims or evidence as final analytical content
Research Agent may produce
                                                   * ACT
                                                   * EVD
                                                   * PRV
                                                   * optional draft CLM
Analysis Agent may produce
                                                   * ACT
                                                   * CLM
                                                   * CNF
                                                   * PRV
Verification Agent may produce
                                                   * VRF
                                                   * optional verification diagnostics
                                                   * optional dispute/conflict records
Memory Agent may produce
                                                   * admission results
                                                   * storage metadata
                                                   * duplicate/conflict linkage metadata
                                                   * retrieval bundles
                                                   * not original analysis claims unless acting under a distinct explicit role
This prevents role confusion.
________________


13. Agent Input Validation Rules
Every agent should validate its input bundle before execution.
Checks should include:
                                                   * bundle shape valid
                                                   * required object types present
                                                   * target operation allowed for this role
                                                   * references sufficiently resolved
                                                   * task status admissible
                                                   * storage/memory context accessible where needed
If input validation fails, the agent should reject the bundle rather than attempting undefined behavior.
________________


14. Retry Semantics
Each agent should specify retry behavior.
Coordinator
May retry routing or reassign to alternative agent if downstream failure occurs.
Research Agent
May retry on transient source or resolution failure.
Analysis Agent
May retry on temporary dependency failure, but not on semantic insufficiency without changed context.
Verification Agent
May retry if comparison context was incomplete, but verification disputes should not be silently retried as if they were transient.
Memory Agent
May retry on transient storage failure, but not on policy rejection.
This distinction is important operationally.
________________


15. Timeout and Constraint Semantics
All agents must respect CST objects or equivalent runtime policy limits.
This includes:
                                                   * max time
                                                   * memory use
                                                   * compute use
                                                   * optional role-specific constraints
If the agent exceeds limits:
                                                   * it must fail explicitly
                                                   * partial semantic output should only be emitted if allowed and clearly marked
No silent truncation.
________________


16. Provenance Responsibilities by Agent
Each agent must append provenance appropriately.
Coordinator
Provenance for orchestration state changes.
Research Agent
Provenance for source extraction and evidence emission.
Analysis Agent
Provenance linking claims back to evidence and source bundles.
Verification Agent
Provenance linking verification result to evaluated target bundle and method.
Memory Agent
Provenance linking stored bundle to admission event and storage tier placement.
This ensures full semantic lineage.
________________


17. Agent Contracts in Repo Terms
These contracts should live under something like:
packages/agent-contracts/
├── base/
├── coordinator/
├── research/
├── analysis/
├── verification/
└── memory/
Each role package should define:
                                                   * role interface
                                                   * allowed message classes
                                                   * input bundle requirements
                                                   * output bundle schema
                                                   * lifecycle state model
                                                   * failure semantics
                                                   * capability declaration
                                                   * observability fields
________________


18. Observability Requirements per Agent
Every agent should emit at least:
                                                   * task ID
                                                   * bundle ID
                                                   * agent ID
                                                   * role
                                                   * input accepted/rejected
                                                   * execution start time
                                                   * execution end time
                                                   * result status
                                                   * failure category if any
                                                   * objects produced count
                                                   * verification/admission outcome if downstream
This makes debugging and runtime analysis possible.
________________


19. Success Criteria per Agent
Each agent needs a role-specific definition of success.
Coordinator success
Workflow is advanced to verified reuse or verified storage without unresolved critical errors.
Research success
Evidence/provenance bundle emitted and admissible for downstream analysis.
Analysis success
Claim bundle emitted with sufficient semantic structure for verification.
Verification success
Explicit VRF status emitted and bound to correct semantic target.
Memory success
Correct reuse, deduplication, or storage-tier decision emitted and persisted as appropriate.
________________


20. Final Summary
The first five agents of the AASL-native Atrahasis runtime should be governed by explicit contracts that define:
                                                   * what each agent may receive
                                                   * what each agent may produce
                                                   * what semantic roles each agent is allowed to perform
                                                   * how each agent transitions through lifecycle state
                                                   * how failures are classified
                                                   * how memory is consulted or updated
                                                   * how provenance is appended
                                                   * how verification and trust boundaries are respected
These contracts turn the runtime from a loose set of roles into a rigorously defined semantic execution system.
________________


The next thing we should work on is:
The exact AACP + AASL message contracts for the first runtime
That means defining the specific message envelopes and payload schemas for:
                                                   * task submission
                                                   * task assignment
                                                   * task result
                                                   * verification request
                                                   * verification result
                                                   * memory lookup
                                                   * memory hit/miss
                                                   * storage admission
                                                   * error and state updates
That is the cleanest next implementation step because the agent contracts are now defined, and the next layer is the exact wire-level communication contract connecting all of them.
Exact AACP + AASL Message Contracts for the First Runtime
With the first five agent contracts defined, the next implementation-critical layer is the exact message contract system that connects them. These contracts define how semantic work moves through the first AASL-native Atrahasis runtime. Up to now, we established that all internal communication should use:
                                                   * AACP as the protocol envelope
                                                   * AASL as the semantic payload
This step now turns that principle into concrete runtime contracts.
The goal is to define the message families that allow:
                                                   * ingress to submit work
                                                   * coordinator to assign work
                                                   * agents to return results
                                                   * verification to evaluate bundles
                                                   * memory to perform lookups and admissions
                                                   * services to emit state and error updates
This is the exact wire-level execution fabric of the first runtime.
________________


1. Core Message Architecture
Every internal runtime message should follow one universal structure:
AACP Message
 ├── HEADER
 └── PAYLOAD
Where:
                                                   * the HEADER carries routing, identity, workflow, and transport metadata
                                                   * the PAYLOAD carries AASL semantic objects and bundle metadata
This must be true for every first-runtime interaction.
________________


2. Universal Message Header
Every message in the first runtime should include the following required header fields:
                                                   * protocol_version
                                                   * aasl_version
                                                   * ontology_version
                                                   * message_id
                                                   * conversation_id
                                                   * workflow_id
                                                   * parent_message_id
                                                   * sender_id
                                                   * receiver_id
                                                   * message_class
                                                   * payload_encoding
                                                   * timestamp
                                                   * status
Recommended canonical form:
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.000001
 conversation_id:conv.000001
 workflow_id:wf.000001
 parent_message_id:msg.000000
 sender_id:svc.ingress.01
 receiver_id:ag.coordination.01
 message_class:task_submission
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
 timestamp:2026-03-08T12:00:00Z
 status:pending
}
This header is the transport contract that every service and agent must understand.
________________


3. Universal Payload Structure
For the first runtime, every payload should contain a semantic bundle wrapper around the actual AASL objects.
Recommended structure:
PAYLOAD{
 BND{
  bundle_id:bnd.000001
  bundle_type:task_bundle
  source_task_id:t.climate.001
  produced_by:svc.ingress.01
  validation_state:validated
  canonical_state:canonical
  verification_state:unverified
  storage_tier:none
 }
 ...
AASL objects...
}
This means messages do not send arbitrary loose object lists. They send a bundle plus its semantic contents.
________________


4. First Runtime Message Families
The first runtime should define exactly these message classes:
                                                   1. task_submission
                                                   2. task_assignment
                                                   3. task_result
                                                   4. verification_request
                                                   5. verification_result
                                                   6. memory_lookup_request
                                                   7. memory_lookup_result
                                                   8. memory_admission_request
                                                   9. memory_admission_result
                                                   10. state_update
                                                   11. error_report
These are enough to support the full first-runtime loop without ambiguity.
________________


5. task_submission
This is the ingress-to-coordinator message.
Purpose
Used when external input has already been compiled into a semantic task bundle and is being handed to the Coordinator Agent.
Sender
                                                   * svc.ingress.*
Receiver
                                                   * ag.coordination.*
Required payload contents
                                                   * one BND of type task_bundle
                                                   * one primary TSK
                                                   * optional CST
                                                   * optional referenced DS
                                                   * optional provenance or source context
Example
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.100001
 conversation_id:conv.100001
 workflow_id:wf.100001
 parent_message_id:none
 sender_id:svc.ingress.01
 receiver_id:ag.coordination.01
 message_class:task_submission
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
 timestamp:2026-03-08T12:00:00Z
 status:pending
}


PAYLOAD{
 BND{
  bundle_id:bnd.task.100001
  bundle_type:task_bundle
  source_task_id:t.climate.001
  produced_by:svc.ingress.01
  validation_state:validated
  canonical_state:canonical
  verification_state:unverified
  storage_tier:none
 }


 TSK{id:t.climate.001 op:analyze target:ds.climate.44 priority:high}
 CST{target:t.climate.001 max_time_ms:10000}
 DS{id:ds.climate.44 type:dataset source:archive.noaa}
}

________________
6. task_assignment
This is the coordinator-to-agent work request.
Purpose
Used by the Coordinator to assign work to Research or Analysis agents.
Sender
                                                   * ag.coordination.*
Receiver
                                                   * ag.research.*
                                                   * ag.analysis.*
Required payload contents
                                                   * one BND of type assignment_bundle
                                                   * one primary TSK
                                                   * optional supporting objects
                                                   * optional memory context objects
                                                   * optional constraints
Example
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.100002
 conversation_id:conv.100001
 workflow_id:wf.100001
 parent_message_id:msg.100001
 sender_id:ag.coordination.01
 receiver_id:ag.research.01
 message_class:task_assignment
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
 timestamp:2026-03-08T12:00:03Z
 status:pending
}


PAYLOAD{
 BND{
  bundle_id:bnd.assign.100002
  bundle_type:assignment_bundle
  source_task_id:t.climate.001
  produced_by:ag.coordination.01
  validation_state:validated
  canonical_state:canonical
  verification_state:unverified
  storage_tier:none
 }


 TSK{id:t.climate.001 op:analyze target:ds.climate.44 priority:high}
 DS{id:ds.climate.44 type:dataset source:archive.noaa}
 CST{target:t.climate.001 max_time_ms:10000}
}

________________
7. task_result
This is the agent-to-coordinator output message.
Purpose
Used by Research or Analysis agents to return semantic output bundles.
Sender
                                                   * ag.research.*
                                                   * ag.analysis.*
Receiver
                                                   * ag.coordination.*
Required payload contents
                                                   * one BND of type result_bundle
                                                   * produced objects such as ACT, EVD, CLM, CNF, PRV
                                                   * execution result metadata in the bundle wrapper
Example
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.100003
 conversation_id:conv.100001
 workflow_id:wf.100001
 parent_message_id:msg.100002
 sender_id:ag.analysis.01
 receiver_id:ag.coordination.01
 message_class:task_result
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
 timestamp:2026-03-08T12:00:10Z
 status:completed
}


PAYLOAD{
 BND{
  bundle_id:bnd.result.100003
  bundle_type:result_bundle
  source_task_id:t.climate.001
  produced_by:ag.analysis.01
  validation_state:validated
  canonical_state:canonical
  verification_state:pending
  storage_tier:none
 }


 ACT{id:a.analyze.201 actor:ag.analysis.01 op:analyze target:ds.climate.44}
 CLM{id:c.correlation.001 type:correlation subject:var.temp object:var.co2}
 CNF{target:c.correlation.001 val:0.92}
 PRV{target:c.correlation.001 source:dataset}
}

________________
8. verification_request
This is the coordinator-to-verification message.
Purpose
Used by the Coordinator to request evaluation of a result bundle.
Sender
                                                   * ag.coordination.*
Receiver
                                                   * ag.verification.*
Required payload contents
                                                   * one BND of type verification_candidate_bundle
                                                   * original TSK
                                                   * candidate claim/result objects
                                                   * supporting evidence/provenance objects
Example
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.100004
 conversation_id:conv.100001
 workflow_id:wf.100001
 parent_message_id:msg.100003
 sender_id:ag.coordination.01
 receiver_id:ag.verification.01
 message_class:verification_request
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
 timestamp:2026-03-08T12:00:12Z
 status:pending
}


PAYLOAD{
 BND{
  bundle_id:bnd.verify.100004
  bundle_type:verification_candidate_bundle
  source_task_id:t.climate.001
  produced_by:ag.coordination.01
  validation_state:validated
  canonical_state:canonical
  verification_state:pending
  storage_tier:none
 }


 TSK{id:t.climate.001 op:analyze target:ds.climate.44 priority:high}
 CLM{id:c.correlation.001 type:correlation subject:var.temp object:var.co2}
 CNF{target:c.correlation.001 val:0.92}
 PRV{target:c.correlation.001 source:dataset}
}

________________
9. verification_result
This is the verification-to-coordinator trust response.
Purpose
Used by the Verification Agent to return a verification decision.
Sender
                                                   * ag.verification.*
Receiver
                                                   * ag.coordination.*
Required payload contents
                                                   * one BND of type verification_result_bundle
                                                   * one or more VRF
                                                   * optional dispute diagnostics
Example
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.100005
 conversation_id:conv.100001
 workflow_id:wf.100001
 parent_message_id:msg.100004
 sender_id:ag.verification.01
 receiver_id:ag.coordination.01
 message_class:verification_result
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
 timestamp:2026-03-08T12:00:16Z
 status:verified
}


PAYLOAD{
 BND{
  bundle_id:bnd.verify_result.100005
  bundle_type:verification_result_bundle
  source_task_id:t.climate.001
  produced_by:ag.verification.01
  validation_state:validated
  canonical_state:canonical
  verification_state:verified
  storage_tier:none
 }


 VRF{target:c.correlation.001 status:verified method:consensus}
 PRV{target:c.correlation.001 source:agent}
}

________________
10. memory_lookup_request
This is the coordinator-to-memory pre-execution check.
Purpose
Used to determine whether reusable semantic knowledge already exists.
Sender
                                                   * ag.coordination.*
Receiver
                                                   * ag.memory.*
Required payload contents
                                                   * one BND of type memory_lookup_bundle
                                                   * task context
                                                   * target identifiers
                                                   * optional lookup hints such as claim type or canonical hash candidate
Example
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.100006
 conversation_id:conv.100001
 workflow_id:wf.100001
 parent_message_id:msg.100001
 sender_id:ag.coordination.01
 receiver_id:ag.memory.01
 message_class:memory_lookup_request
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
 timestamp:2026-03-08T12:00:01Z
 status:pending
}


PAYLOAD{
 BND{
  bundle_id:bnd.lookup.100006
  bundle_type:memory_lookup_bundle
  source_task_id:t.climate.001
  produced_by:ag.coordination.01
  validation_state:validated
  canonical_state:canonical
  verification_state:unverified
  storage_tier:none
 }


 TSK{id:t.climate.001 op:analyze target:ds.climate.44 priority:high}
 DS{id:ds.climate.44 type:dataset source:archive.noaa}
}

________________
11. memory_lookup_result
This is the memory-to-coordinator reuse answer.
Purpose
Used to report a hit, miss, or partial reusable bundle.
Sender
                                                   * ag.memory.*
Receiver
                                                   * ag.coordination.*
Required payload contents
                                                   * one BND of type memory_lookup_result_bundle
                                                   * explicit hit/miss metadata
                                                   * optional reusable semantic bundle objects
Example hit
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.100007
 conversation_id:conv.100001
 workflow_id:wf.100001
 parent_message_id:msg.100006
 sender_id:ag.memory.01
 receiver_id:ag.coordination.01
 message_class:memory_lookup_result
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
 timestamp:2026-03-08T12:00:02Z
 status:completed
}


PAYLOAD{
 BND{
  bundle_id:bnd.lookup_result.100007
  bundle_type:memory_lookup_result_bundle
  source_task_id:t.climate.001
  produced_by:ag.memory.01
  validation_state:validated
  canonical_state:canonical
  verification_state:verified
  storage_tier:verified
  lookup_status:hit
 }


 CLM{id:c.correlation.001 type:correlation subject:var.temp object:var.co2}
 CNF{target:c.correlation.001 val:0.92}
 VRF{target:c.correlation.001 status:verified method:consensus}
}
Miss would carry lookup_status:miss and no reusable semantic result objects.
________________


12. memory_admission_request
This is the coordinator-to-memory post-verification storage request.
Purpose
Used to request storage of a candidate verified bundle.
Sender
                                                   * ag.coordination.*
Receiver
                                                   * ag.memory.*
Required payload contents
                                                   * one BND of type memory_admission_bundle
                                                   * canonical result objects
                                                   * verification record(s)
                                                   * provenance objects
                                                   * optional canonical hash
Example
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.100008
 conversation_id:conv.100001
 workflow_id:wf.100001
 parent_message_id:msg.100005
 sender_id:ag.coordination.01
 receiver_id:ag.memory.01
 message_class:memory_admission_request
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
 timestamp:2026-03-08T12:00:17Z
 status:pending
}


PAYLOAD{
 BND{
  bundle_id:bnd.admission.100008
  bundle_type:memory_admission_bundle
  source_task_id:t.climate.001
  produced_by:ag.coordination.01
  validation_state:validated
  canonical_state:canonical
  verification_state:verified
  storage_tier:pending
 }


 CLM{id:c.correlation.001 type:correlation subject:var.temp object:var.co2}
 CNF{target:c.correlation.001 val:0.92}
 VRF{target:c.correlation.001 status:verified method:consensus}
 PRV{target:c.correlation.001 source:dataset}
}

________________
13. memory_admission_result
This is the memory-to-coordinator admission decision.
Purpose
Used to return admission status, tier placement, duplicate resolution, or rejection.
Sender
                                                   * ag.memory.*
Receiver
                                                   * ag.coordination.*
Required payload contents
                                                   * one BND of type memory_admission_result_bundle
                                                   * admission result metadata
                                                   * optional duplicate or supersession markers
Example
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.100009
 conversation_id:conv.100001
 workflow_id:wf.100001
 parent_message_id:msg.100008
 sender_id:ag.memory.01
 receiver_id:ag.coordination.01
 message_class:memory_admission_result
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
 timestamp:2026-03-08T12:00:18Z
 status:completed
}


PAYLOAD{
 BND{
  bundle_id:bnd.admission_result.100009
  bundle_type:memory_admission_result_bundle
  source_task_id:t.climate.001
  produced_by:ag.memory.01
  validation_state:validated
  canonical_state:canonical
  verification_state:verified
  storage_tier:verified
  admission_status:accepted
 }
}
Possible statuses:
                                                   * accepted
                                                   * duplicate_reused
                                                   * superseded_existing
                                                   * rejected
                                                   * quarantined
________________


14. state_update
This is a general operational update message.
Purpose
Used by any service or agent to emit nonterminal workflow progress.
Sender
                                                   * any runtime participant
Receiver
                                                   * coordinator
                                                   * operator console
                                                   * API layer
                                                   * observability pipeline
Payload contents
                                                   * one BND of type state_update_bundle
                                                   * workflow/task state metadata
                                                   * optional related object IDs
Example
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.100010
 conversation_id:conv.100001
 workflow_id:wf.100001

 sender_id:ag.research.01
 receiver_id:ag.coordination.01

}

  produced_by:ag.research.01
  validation_state:not_applicable
  canonical_state:not_applicable
  verification_state:not_applicable
  execution_phase:extracting
 }
}

15. error_report
This is the universal failure message.
Purpose
Used when a service or agent cannot continue a workflow step.
Sender
                                                   * any runtime participant
Receiver
                                                   * coordinator or upstream caller
Payload contents
                                                   * one BND of type error_bundle
                                                   * structured error metadata
                                                   * optional related object IDs
                                                   * retry recommendation
Example
HEADER{
 protocol_version:1.0.0
 aasl_version:1.0.0
 ontology_version:1.0
 message_id:msg.100011
 conversation_id:conv.100001
 workflow_id:wf.100001
 parent_message_id:msg.100002
 sender_id:ag.research.01
 receiver_id:ag.coordination.01
 message_class:error_report
 payload_encoding:AASL-T
 timestamp:2026-03-08T12:00:06Z
 status:failed
}


PAYLOAD{
 BND{
  bundle_id:bnd.error.100011
  bundle_type:error_bundle
  source_task_id:t.climate.001
  produced_by:ag.research.01
  failure_category:source_unavailable
  retry_allowed:true
 }
}

________________
16. Standard Bundle Types
For the first runtime, the system should formally recognize these bundle types:
                                                   * task_bundle
                                                   * assignment_bundle
                                                   * result_bundle
                                                   * verification_candidate_bundle
                                                   * verification_result_bundle
                                                   * memory_lookup_bundle
                                                   * memory_lookup_result_bundle
                                                   * memory_admission_bundle
                                                   * memory_admission_result_bundle
                                                   * state_update_bundle
                                                   * error_bundle
This prevents services from inventing ad hoc payload shapes.
________________


17. Header Rules for All Messages
These runtime-wide rules should apply:
                                                   1. message_id must always be unique.
                                                   2. workflow_id must remain constant for one end-to-end task lifecycle.
                                                   3. conversation_id groups related external interaction scope.
                                                   4. parent_message_id must point to the message that directly caused this message.
                                                   5. message_class must match payload purpose.
                                                   6. status must reflect message outcome state, not arbitrary human wording.
                                                   7. sender_id and receiver_id must be concrete runtime identities.
This guarantees traceability.
________________


18. Payload Rules for All Messages
These runtime-wide payload rules should apply:
                                                   1. Every payload must include exactly one top-level BND.
                                                   2. All semantic objects in the payload must belong to that bundle context.
                                                   3. Payloads must be parseable and at least minimally validated before transmission.
                                                   4. Noncanonical draft bundles must be explicitly marked in bundle metadata.
                                                   5. Trusted claims must not be transmitted as trusted unless accompanied by valid verification state.
                                                   6. Memory admission requests must carry canonical content only.
This keeps the runtime semantically clean.
________________


19. Contract Ownership in the Repo
These message contracts should live primarily in:
packages/aacp-contracts/
Recommended structure:
packages/aacp-contracts/
├── header/
├── bundle-types/
├── message-classes/
├── task-submission/
├── task-assignment/
├── task-result/
├── verification/
├── memory/
├── state/
└── error/
Shared AASL object typings remain in:
packages/aasl-core/
And agent-specific usage constraints remain in:
packages/agent-contracts/

________________
20. Validation Expectations for Messages
Every message should be validated at three levels before acceptance:
Transport-level
                                                   * header complete
                                                   * message class known
                                                   * sender/receiver admissible
Bundle-level
                                                   * bundle type valid for message class
                                                   * required bundle metadata present
Semantic-level
                                                   * payload objects valid AASL
                                                   * required object types present
                                                   * references sufficiently resolved
                                                   * validation/canonical/verification states admissible for the receiving role
This makes message handling rigorous from day one.
________________


21. End-to-End Example Flow
The first runtime’s complete message chain for a new task should be:
                                                   1. task_submission
                                                   2. memory_lookup_request
                                                   3. memory_lookup_result
                                                   4. if miss:
                                                   * task_assignment to Research
                                                   * task_result from Research
                                                   * task_assignment to Analysis
                                                   * task_result from Analysis
                                                   * verification_request
                                                   * verification_result
                                                   * memory_admission_request
                                                   * memory_admission_result
                                                   5. optional state_update messages throughout
                                                   6. error_report at any failure point
This is the canonical semantic workflow of the first runtime.
________________


22. Final Summary
The first runtime should use a strict AACP + AASL message system where every message contains:
                                                   * a protocol HEADER
                                                   * a bundle-centered AASL PAYLOAD
The runtime must support these concrete message classes:
                                                   * task_submission
                                                   * task_assignment
                                                   * task_result
                                                   * verification_request
                                                   * verification_result
                                                   * memory_lookup_request
                                                   * memory_lookup_result
                                                   * memory_admission_request
                                                   * memory_admission_result
                                                   * state_update
                                                   * error_report
These contracts are the actual wire-level execution language of the first AASL-native Atrahasis runtime.
________________


The next thing we should work on is:
the exact storage schema and semantic bundle model for the first runtime
That means defining:
                                                   * tables/collections
                                                   * bundle persistence structures
                                                   * object/reference storage shapes
                                                   * canonical hash storage
                                                   * verification storage
                                                   * provenance storage
                                                   * retrieval indexes
That is the right next step because the runtime process model, agent contracts, and message contracts are now defined, and the next implementation boundary is exactly how semantic knowledge is persisted and retrieved.
Exact Storage Schema and Semantic Bundle Model for the First Runtime
With the runtime process model, agent contracts, and AACP + AASL message contracts now defined, the next implementation boundary is the exact persistence model. This is where AASL stops being only an in-memory semantic substrate and becomes a durable operational knowledge layer.
The first runtime storage design must support five things at the same time:
                                                   * persistence of full semantic bundles
                                                   * persistence of individual AASL objects
                                                   * persistence of references and graph relationships
                                                   * persistence of provenance and verification state
                                                   * fast retrieval for memory-first execution and semantic reuse
This design is for the first complete working runtime, not the final planetary-scale Atrahasis store. But it must still be architecturally correct so that later scaling does not require discarding the semantic model.
________________


1. Storage Design Principle
The first runtime should use a bundle-centric, object-indexed storage model.
That means the storage system treats the semantic bundle as the primary operational unit while also indexing and storing every individual object inside the bundle for graph traversal and query.
So there are two simultaneous truths:
                                                   * the bundle is the main workflow and memory unit
                                                   * the object is the main semantic and query unit
This duality is essential.
If you store only documents, you lose semantic flexibility.
If you store only isolated objects, you lose execution context, provenance grouping, and workflow cohesion.
So the first runtime store must preserve both.
________________


2. Core Persistence Layers
The first runtime storage schema should be divided into these logical layers:
                                                   1. Bundle Store
                                                   2. Document Store
                                                   3. Object Store
                                                   4. Reference Store
                                                   5. Provenance Store
                                                   6. Verification Store
                                                   7. Execution Store
                                                   8. Index Layer
                                                   9. Tier / Admission State Layer
These do not necessarily need to be separate databases, but they must be separate schema domains.
________________


3. Semantic Bundle Model
The semantic bundle is the main storage unit moving through the runtime.
A bundle represents one coherent semantic package associated with a task lifecycle event.
Examples:
                                                   * task submission bundle
                                                   * research result bundle
                                                   * analysis result bundle
                                                   * verification result bundle
                                                   * memory admission bundle
                                                   * reusable memory bundle
A bundle must contain:
                                                   * bundle identity
                                                   * workflow/task association
                                                   * producing actor/service
                                                   * semantic objects
                                                   * semantic references
                                                   * lifecycle state
                                                   * validation/canonical/verification state
                                                   * provenance linkage
                                                   * storage tier intent
                                                   * canonical hash information
                                                   * admission metadata
So the bundle is not just a list of objects. It is the operational semantic container.
________________


4. Bundle Schema
The first runtime should define a formal bundle record with fields like these:
Bundle Identity Fields
                                                   * bundle_id
                                                   * bundle_type
                                                   * source_task_id
                                                   * workflow_id
                                                   * conversation_id
Production Fields
                                                   * produced_by
                                                   * produced_at
                                                   * parent_bundle_id
                                                   * parent_message_id
State Fields
                                                   * execution_status
                                                   * validation_state
                                                   * canonical_state
                                                   * verification_state
                                                   * admission_state
                                                   * storage_tier
Integrity Fields
                                                   * canonical_hash
                                                   * artifact_checksum
                                                   * optional signature_status
Context Fields
                                                   * document_id
                                                   * primary_target_id
                                                   * primary_claim_id
                                                   * primary_dataset_id
Audit Fields
                                                   * created_at
                                                   * updated_at
                                                   * supersedes_bundle_id
                                                   * superseded_by_bundle_id
This bundle record becomes the root metadata row/document for all semantic bundle operations.
________________


5. Bundle Type Taxonomy
For the first runtime, the store should recognize these bundle types as first-class:
                                                   * task_bundle
                                                   * assignment_bundle
                                                   * result_bundle
                                                   * verification_candidate_bundle
                                                   * verification_result_bundle
                                                   * memory_lookup_bundle
                                                   * memory_lookup_result_bundle
                                                   * memory_admission_bundle
                                                   * memory_admission_result_bundle
                                                   * state_update_bundle
                                                   * error_bundle
Each type should map to expected object patterns and retrieval rules.
For example:
                                                   * result_bundle usually contains ACT, CLM, CNF, PRV
                                                   * verification_result_bundle usually contains VRF
                                                   * memory_lookup_result_bundle may contain reusable CLM, CNF, VRF
This makes storage semantically aware.
________________


6. Bundle Lifecycle States
Each bundle should move through explicit states.
Recommended first-runtime bundle lifecycle:
                                                   * created
                                                   * parsed
                                                   * validated
                                                   * canonicalized
                                                   * verification_pending
                                                   * verified
                                                   * rejected
                                                   * quarantined
                                                   * admitted
