                                                   * superseded
                                                   * archived
This lifecycle should be persisted, not just tracked transiently in memory.
That allows:
                                                   * recovery after service restart
                                                   * auditability
                                                   * replay/debug
                                                   * tier movement
________________


7. Bundle Store
The Bundle Store is the highest-level operational table/collection.
It should store one record per bundle.
Responsibilities:
                                                   * identify bundle
                                                   * track lifecycle state
                                                   * track workflow relations
                                                   * track tier placement
                                                   * track bundle-level integrity
                                                   * support retrieval of full bundle context
Think of this as the runtime execution and memory envelope index.
A bundle record should not store every object inline as the only representation. It should reference object membership, but may also cache serialized canonical artifact content for speed and durability.
________________


8. Bundle Membership Table / Collection
Because each bundle contains multiple semantic objects, the storage model should include an explicit membership mapping.
This mapping should record:
                                                   * bundle_id
                                                   * object_id
                                                   * object_type
                                                   * membership_role
                                                   * object_order
                                                   * is_primary
membership_role is important because the same object may play different roles in a bundle, such as:
                                                   * primary task
                                                   * supporting evidence
                                                   * produced claim
                                                   * attached verification
                                                   * attached provenance
                                                   * attached diagnostic object
This makes bundle reconstruction deterministic.
________________


9. Document Store
The Document Store persists full canonical AASL artifacts.
Each document record should store:
                                                   * document_id
                                                   * bundle_id or originating bundle relation
                                                   * aasl_version
                                                   * ontology_version
                                                   * encoding
                                                   * canonical .aas payload or storage reference
                                                   * artifact checksum
                                                   * canonical hash summary
                                                   * created/updated timestamps
                                                   * storage tier
                                                   * source import metadata
This is the durable artifact view.
Even though the runtime works bundle-first, preserving full documents matters for:
                                                   * export
                                                   * audit
                                                   * human inspection
                                                   * round-trip durability
                                                   * later federation
________________


10. Object Store
The Object Store persists each semantic object individually.
Every object record should include:
Identity
                                                   * object_id
                                                   * object_type
Semantic Fields
                                                   * normalized field payload
                                                   * typed field payload if implemented separately
                                                   * canonical field order snapshot or canonical serialization
Context
                                                   * document_id
                                                   * bundle_id (originating or first-emitted bundle)
                                                   * current tier
                                                   * lifecycle state
Integrity
                                                   * object canonical hash
                                                   * object validation state
                                                   * object canonical state
Audit
                                                   * created_at
                                                   * updated_at
                                                   * supersession linkage if versioned
This store makes AASL queryable as a semantic graph rather than just a file archive.
________________


11. Object Payload Representation
For the first runtime, each object should have both:
                                                   1. a normalized field structure for queryability
                                                   2. a canonical serialized representation for hashing/export consistency
So an object record should conceptually hold:
                                                   * object_id
                                                   * object_type
                                                   * field_map
                                                   * canonical_text
                                                   * object_hash
This is important because:
                                                   * queries need field access
                                                   * hashing and export need stable serialization
Do not force the system to reconstruct canonical text from scratch every single time if it can be stored safely after validation/canonicalization.
________________


12. Reference Store
Because AASL is reference-native, references need explicit persistence.
Each reference record should include:
                                                   * source_object_id
                                                   * source_object_type
                                                   * field_name
                                                   * target_object_id
                                                   * target_object_type if resolved
                                                   * resolution_status
                                                   * bundle_id
                                                   * document_id
This store supports:
                                                   * inbound reference lookup
                                                   * outbound reference lookup
                                                   * graph traversal
                                                   * unresolved reference detection
                                                   * integrity checking
This should not be inferred ad hoc from object payload every time in production paths.
________________


13. Relationship Semantics in Reference Store
The store should distinguish between generic references and semantic attachments.
Examples:
                                                   * ACT.actor → AGT
                                                   * ACT.target → DS
                                                   * CNF.target → CLM
                                                   * VRF.target → CLM
                                                   * PRV.target → object
So the reference store should support:
                                                   * reference_kind
                                                   * field_name
                                                   * semantic attachment classification
This enables richer retrieval such as:
                                                   * get all confidence attached to claim
                                                   * get all verification attached to claim
                                                   * get provenance chain for object
without repeatedly inferring semantics at query time.
________________


14. Provenance Store
The first runtime must treat provenance as first-class.
The Provenance Store should preserve both:
                                                   * explicit PRV objects
                                                   * storage/runtime lineage metadata
A provenance record should include:
                                                   * provenance_id or object_id if using PRV
                                                   * target_object_id
                                                   * source_kind
                                                   * source_reference
                                                   * origin_document_id
                                                   * origin_bundle_id
                                                   * produced_by
                                                   * produced_at
                                                   * optional transformation step metadata
This lets the system answer:
                                                   * where did this claim come from
                                                   * what document introduced this evidence
                                                   * which bundle created this semantic result
                                                   * what lineage led to the current canonical object
________________


15. Verification Store
Verification must also be first-class.
The Verification Store should record:
                                                   * verification_id or underlying VRF.object_id
                                                   * target_object_id
                                                   * verification_status
                                                   * verification_method
                                                   * verifier_id
                                                   * verification_time
                                                   * target canonical hash at time of verification
                                                   * optional dispute metadata
                                                   * bundle and document linkage
This store is critical because verification drives:
                                                   * trust tier promotion
                                                   * memory reuse decisions
                                                   * query filtering
                                                   * conflict handling
The Verification Store should make it cheap to ask:
                                                   * is this claim verified
                                                   * what method verified it
                                                   * who verified it
                                                   * is this verification current or superseded
________________


16. Confidence Store
Confidence can be stored either as regular objects in the Object Store plus reference attachment, or with a dedicated supporting index.
For the first runtime, the best model is:
                                                   * CNF remains a standard object in Object Store
                                                   * plus an attachment index that makes confidence retrieval cheap
So if needed, keep a Confidence Attachment Index with:
                                                   * target_object_id
                                                   * confidence_object_id
                                                   * confidence_value
                                                   * bundle/document linkage
This speeds up one of the most common semantic lookups.
________________


17. Execution Store
The first runtime needs to preserve operational history, not just semantic artifacts.
The Execution Store should track workflow and task execution state.
A record should include:
                                                   * workflow_id
                                                   * conversation_id
                                                   * task_id
                                                   * bundle_id
                                                   * current_status
                                                   * current_owner
                                                   * started_at
                                                   * completed_at
                                                   * verification_required
                                                   * verification_completed
                                                   * memory_lookup_status
                                                   * admission_status
                                                   * error_state if any
This store is essential for:
                                                   * task replay
                                                   * debugging
                                                   * observability
                                                   * operator console views
                                                   * end-to-end workflow inspection
________________


18. Tier State Store
Because the first runtime supports draft, canonical, and verified tiers, the store needs explicit tier state.
A tier state model should include:
                                                   * draft
                                                   * canonical
                                                   * verified
                                                   * quarantined
                                                   * archived
Tier membership should apply at least to:
                                                   * bundles
                                                   * documents
                                                   * objects where relevant
The system should record:
                                                   * current tier
                                                   * prior tier
                                                   * promotion time
                                                   * promotion source
                                                   * rejection or quarantine reason
This makes trust progression explicit and auditable.
________________


19. Admission State Model
Tier is not enough by itself. Admission state should also be tracked.
Recommended values:
                                                   * pending
                                                   * accepted
                                                   * rejected
                                                   * duplicate_reused
                                                   * superseded_existing
                                                   * quarantined
This is especially important for memory admission requests.
For example, a bundle may be:
                                                   * canonical
                                                   * verified
                                                   * but still quarantined due to policy or conflict
That must be representable.
________________


20. Canonical Hash Storage
Canonical hash is central to reuse and deduplication.
The storage system should store canonical hashes at multiple levels:
Bundle-level canonical hash
Represents the semantic identity of the full bundle.
Object-level canonical hash
Represents the semantic identity of an object.
Target-specific hash linkage
For verification records and conflict analysis.
A canonical hash index should support:
                                                   * exact lookup by hash
                                                   * duplicate detection
                                                   * equivalence grouping
                                                   * memory reuse lookup
This is one of the most important indexes in the entire runtime.
________________


21. Duplicate and Equivalence Store
The first runtime should explicitly track duplicates/equivalence, not just infer them on the fly.
This store should record:
                                                   * canonical hash
                                                   * primary object or bundle ID
                                                   * equivalent object/bundle IDs
                                                   * equivalence reason
                                                   * current preferred representative
                                                   * detection time
This allows the Memory Agent to say:
                                                   * this result already exists
                                                   * this is equivalent to existing canonical knowledge
                                                   * reuse existing verified bundle instead of recomputing
That is the semantic cache mechanism in persistent form.
________________


22. Supersession and Version Store
Knowledge evolves, so supersession must be explicit.
A supersession record should include:
                                                   * old_object_id or old_bundle_id
                                                   * new_object_id or new_bundle_id
                                                   * supersession_reason
                                                   * superseded_at
                                                   * superseded_by
                                                   * whether replacement is authoritative
This is necessary for:
                                                   * version history
                                                   * replay protection
                                                   * current-vs-historical retrieval
                                                   * operator inspection
Without it, the store becomes temporally incoherent.
________________


23. Conflict Store
Conflicts should be explicit records, not hidden conditions.
A conflict record should include:
                                                   * conflict ID
                                                   * conflict type
                                                   * involved object/bundle IDs
                                                   * involved hashes
                                                   * detected_at
                                                   * status (open, resolved, disputed, ignored)
                                                   * optional governing decision
Conflict types may include:
                                                   * duplicate ID conflict
                                                   * conflicting field values
                                                   * conflicting verification records
                                                   * conflicting active canonical candidate
                                                   * unresolved supersession ambiguity
The first runtime may keep conflict resolution simple, but it must preserve conflict visibility.
________________


24. Retrieval Indexes
The first runtime needs explicit indexes for fast retrieval.
At minimum:
Bundle Indexes
                                                   * by bundle_id
                                                   * by bundle_type
                                                   * by source_task_id
                                                   * by workflow_id
                                                   * by storage_tier
                                                   * by verification_state
Object Indexes
                                                   * by object_id
                                                   * by object_type
                                                   * by document_id
                                                   * by bundle_id
                                                   * by lifecycle/tier state
Semantic Indexes
                                                   * by claim type
                                                   * by role
                                                   * by operation
                                                   * by verification status
                                                   * by canonical hash
                                                   * by primary target ID
Relationship Indexes
                                                   * inbound/outbound references
                                                   * attachment indexes for CNF, PRV, VRF
These indexes are required for memory-first execution and fast query.
________________


25. Primary Semantic Retrieval Shapes
The store should support these retrieval shapes directly:
                                                   1. Bundle retrieval
                                                   * whole bundle with member objects
                                                   2. Object retrieval
                                                   * single object plus state and membership
                                                   3. Claim bundle retrieval
                                                   * claim plus attached confidence, provenance, verification
                                                   4. Memory reuse retrieval
                                                   * latest reusable verified bundle for semantic target
                                                   5. Workflow retrieval
                                                   * all bundles and state transitions for one workflow
                                                   6. Conflict retrieval
                                                   * conflicting records and their current disposition
The schema should be optimized for these actual runtime needs.
________________


26. Bundle Reconstruction Rules
Because objects are stored separately, the store must support deterministic bundle reconstruction.
Given a bundle_id, reconstruction should return:
                                                   * bundle metadata
                                                   * member objects in canonical or stored order
                                                   * attached references
                                                   * provenance attachments
                                                   * verification attachments
                                                   * current state metadata
This is necessary for:
                                                   * replaying workflow steps
                                                   * rehydrating runtime state
                                                   * exporting .aas
                                                   * operator inspection
                                                   * federation later
________________


27. Rehydration Model
The storage model must support hydration back into runtime.
A rehydration request should be able to load:
                                                   * a whole bundle
                                                   * an object neighborhood
                                                   * a claim bundle
                                                   * a workflow trace
                                                   * all verified knowledge for a target
That means the store must preserve enough semantic context so runtime does not need to guess relationships after load.
Hydration should return:
                                                   * objects
                                                   * references
                                                   * bundle context
                                                   * state context
                                                   * provenance/verification attachments
This is what makes storage and runtime a coherent loop.
________________


28. First Physical Implementation Shape
For the first runtime, the cleanest practical backend pattern is:
                                                   * relational store for normalized metadata, object fields, references, workflow state, indexes
                                                   * artifact blob/text store for canonical .aas bundle/document payloads
                                                   * optional in-memory cache for hot bundle and object retrieval
Even if the exact technologies change later, the schema should assume this logical split:
                                                   * structured queryable state
                                                   * canonical serialized artifact durability
That is the right first implementation shape.
________________


29. Transaction Boundaries
The first runtime must define transaction boundaries carefully.
These operations should commit atomically:
Task submission persistence
                                                   * bundle record
                                                   * member objects
                                                   * execution state row
Agent result commit
                                                   * result bundle
                                                   * new objects
                                                   * references
                                                   * provenance records
                                                   * execution state update
Verification commit
                                                   * verification result bundle
                                                   * VRF
                                                   * verification index updates
                                                   * execution state update
Memory admission commit
                                                   * bundle tier/admission update
                                                   * duplicate/equivalence records
                                                   * current representative selection
                                                   * storage commit metadata
This prevents semantic inconsistency.
________________


30. Validation Before Storage
The store must never be a passive dump.
Before committing any bundle into canonical or verified tiers, the storage layer should require:
                                                   * parse success
                                                   * validation success
                                                   * canonicalization success
                                                   * resolved required references
                                                   * admissible verification state if entering verified tier
Draft tier may allow looser standards, but that must be explicit.
So storage integrates tightly with validation and canonicalization.
________________


31. Store APIs
The storage service should expose stable APIs around this schema.
Core API groups:
Bundle APIs
                                                   * create bundle
                                                   * get bundle
                                                   * list bundles by workflow/task/type/state
                                                   * reconstruct bundle
Object APIs
                                                   * get object
                                                   * get objects by type
                                                   * get objects by bundle/document/target
Reference APIs
                                                   * get outbound references
                                                   * get inbound references
                                                   * get attachments
Verification APIs
                                                   * get verification by target
                                                   * get verified latest
                                                   * get disputed records
Memory APIs
                                                   * lookup reusable bundle
                                                   * detect duplicate by canonical hash
                                                   * admit bundle to tier
                                                   * mark supersession/conflict
Workflow APIs
                                                   * get execution trace
                                                   * update workflow state
                                                   * inspect task path
These APIs directly support the runtime services already defined.
________________


32. Proposed Schema Grouping in the Repo
This schema should live conceptually under:
schemas/storage/
Recommended files/modules:
schemas/storage/
├── bundles/
├── documents/
├── objects/
├── references/
├── provenance/
├── verification/
├── execution/
├── conflicts/
├── versions/
└── indexes/
Implementation contracts should then live in:
packages/aasl-storage-contracts/
This keeps formal shape and implementation abstraction separate.
________________


33. Example Bundle Persistence Shape
A stored result bundle in conceptual form should tie together:
                                                   * bundle record:
                                                   * bnd.result.100003
                                                   * member objects:
                                                   * a.analyze.201
                                                   * c.correlation.001
                                                   * cnf.correlation.001
                                                   * prv.correlation.001
                                                   * references:
                                                   * ACT.actor -> ag.analysis.01
                                                   * ACT.target -> ds.climate.44
                                                   * CNF.target -> c.correlation.001
                                                   * PRV.target -> c.correlation.001
                                                   * bundle state:
                                                   * validated
                                                   * canonical
                                                   * verification pending
Then later verification adds:
                                                   * vrf.correlation.001
                                                   * verification state becomes verified
Then memory admission adds:
                                                   * storage tier = verified
                                                   * canonical bundle hash indexed
                                                   * reusable memory representative selected
That is the exact persistence loop the first runtime needs.
________________


34. What This Storage Model Enables
If implemented correctly, this storage schema enables:
                                                   * bundle-centric workflow persistence
                                                   * semantic object queryability
                                                   * exact provenance and verification attachment retrieval
                                                   * memory-first reuse
                                                   * canonical deduplication
                                                   * conflict and version visibility
                                                   * runtime rehydration
                                                   * durable export back to .aas
This is the first true persistent semantic memory model of Atrahasis.
________________


35. Final Summary
The first runtime should use a bundle-centric, object-indexed storage schema composed of:
                                                   * Bundle Store
                                                   * Document Store
                                                   * Object Store
                                                   * Reference Store
                                                   * Provenance Store
                                                   * Verification Store
                                                   * Execution Store
                                                   * Tier / Admission State
                                                   * Duplicate / Equivalence / Conflict / Supersession records
                                                   * retrieval indexes keyed by ID, type, target, state, and canonical hash
The semantic bundle is the primary operational unit, while objects and references are the primary semantic and query units. This dual model preserves workflow cohesion and semantic graph power at the same time.
________________


The next thing we should work on is:
the exact API contract layer for the first runtime
That means defining the external and internal APIs for:
                                                   * ingress submission
                                                   * workflow status
                                                   * semantic query
                                                   * bundle retrieval
                                                   * memory lookup
                                                   * export
                                                   * operator inspection
That is the right next step because the repo, agent contracts, message contracts, and persistence schema are now defined, and the next implementation boundary is how all of this is exposed as callable system interfaces.
Exact API Contract Layer for the First Runtime
With the repo architecture, agent contracts, internal message contracts, and storage schema defined, the next implementation boundary is the API contract layer. This is the layer that makes the first AASL-native Atrahasis runtime callable by external clients, operator tools, internal services, and future automation systems.
The API layer is not the semantic language itself. It is the controlled boundary through which the semantic runtime is exposed. If designed correctly, it will let the rest of the world interact with Atrahasis without breaking the internal rule that all internal knowledge and workflow state is represented as AASL.
This layer answers:
How do clients and services actually call the first runtime, submit work, retrieve semantic results, inspect workflows, and access shared memory?
________________


1. Core API Principle
The API layer must follow one strict rule:
APIs may accept multiple ingress formats, but they must always normalize to AASL internally and expose AASL-native retrieval as a first-class capability.
That means:
                                                   * external users may submit English, markdown, JSON, or files
                                                   * internal runtime APIs operate on AASL bundles and AASL objects
                                                   * external clients may request either:
                                                   * native semantic output
                                                   * human-readable output
                                                   * or both
So the API layer is the translation boundary between:
                                                   * human/application access
                                                   * the AASL-native runtime
________________


2. API Surface Areas
The first runtime should expose six major API domains:
                                                   1. Ingress API
                                                   2. Workflow API
                                                   3. Semantic Query API
                                                   4. Memory API
                                                   5. Export API
                                                   6. Operator / Inspection API
These are enough to expose the full first-runtime loop without leaking low-level implementation details.
________________


3. API Design Philosophy
The API layer should be:
AASL-native internally
All meaningful system operations should resolve to semantic bundle operations.
Workflow-aware
Every API should preserve workflow_id, conversation_id, and traceability metadata.
Versioned
Every endpoint must declare protocol and language versions clearly.
Deterministic
Given the same stored semantic state, the same API calls should yield the same semantic responses.
Introspectable
Clients should be able to see validation, canonicalization, verification, and admission state.
Safe
Trust tier and visibility rules must be enforced consistently.
________________


4. API Transport Style
For the first runtime, the cleanest API approach is:
                                                   * HTTP/JSON for external/public-facing APIs
                                                   * internal service APIs using HTTP or gRPC
                                                   * AACP + AASL messages for agent/service workflow exchange
That means:
                                                   * outside the runtime: conventional web APIs are acceptable
                                                   * inside the runtime: message contracts and bundle contracts are primary
This gives interoperability without compromising the internal architecture.
________________


5. Common API Envelope
All major API responses should use a shared envelope shape.
A response envelope should include:
                                                   * request_id
                                                   * status
                                                   * workflow_id if applicable
                                                   * conversation_id if applicable
                                                   * result_type
                                                   * data
                                                   * diagnostics
                                                   * metadata
Conceptually:
{
  "request_id": "req.100001",
  "status": "success",
  "workflow_id": "wf.100001",
  "conversation_id": "conv.100001",
  "result_type": "semantic_bundle",
  "data": { ... },
  "diagnostics": [],
  "metadata": {
    "aasl_version": "1.0.0",
    "ontology_version": "1.0"
  }
}
This should be consistent across API families.
________________


6. Ingress API
The Ingress API is the external submission boundary.
Its responsibilities are:
                                                   * accept user or system input
                                                   * classify input type
                                                   * optionally compile input to AASL
                                                   * optionally submit compiled task directly into workflow
                                                   * provide preview before execution if requested
The first runtime should expose these ingress operations:
6.1 Submit Task
Accepts raw input or structured task input and starts a workflow.
6.2 Compile Preview
Compiles input into AASL without starting execution.
6.3 Validate Submitted AASL
Accepts native AASL and checks admissibility.
________________


7. POST /ingress/tasks
This is the primary task submission endpoint.
Purpose
Submit a new task into the runtime.
Acceptable inputs
                                                   * plain text
                                                   * markdown
                                                   * JSON task definition
                                                   * native AASL task bundle
Request fields
                                                   * input_type
                                                   * content
                                                   * optional metadata
                                                   * optional constraints
                                                   * optional execute_immediately
                                                   * optional return_mode
Example request:
{
  "input_type": "text",
  "content": "Analyze dataset 44 for correlation between temperature and CO2.",
  "constraints": {
    "max_time_ms": 10000
  },
  "execute_immediately": true,
  "return_mode": "workflow_started"
}
Response
Should return:
                                                   * workflow_id
                                                   * task_id
                                                   * bundle_id
                                                   * initial workflow status
                                                   * compiled semantic summary if available
________________


8. POST /ingress/compile-preview
Purpose
Compile input to AASL without launching the full runtime workflow.
This is useful for:
                                                   * debugging
                                                   * human review
                                                   * authoring assistance
                                                   * operator inspection
Request
Similar to /ingress/tasks but without execution.
Response
Returns:
                                                   * compiled semantic bundle
                                                   * validation results
                                                   * canonicalization results
                                                   * diagnostics
This endpoint is critical for developer and tooling workflows.
________________


9. POST /ingress/validate-aasl
Purpose
Accept native AASL content and validate it.
This supports:
                                                   * manual authoring
                                                   * external semantic producers
                                                   * interoperability testing
Request
                                                   * encoding
                                                   * content
Response
Returns:
                                                   * parse result status
                                                   * validation report
                                                   * canonicalization report
                                                   * admissibility decision
________________


10. Workflow API
The Workflow API exposes execution lifecycle state.
Its responsibilities are:
                                                   * retrieve workflow status
                                                   * retrieve task state
                                                   * retrieve execution history
                                                   * inspect current stage
                                                   * inspect result readiness
                                                   * inspect verification/admission progress
The workflow API should expose:
10.1 Get Workflow Status
10.2 Get Workflow Trace
10.3 Get Latest Result for Workflow
10.4 Retry / Resume where allowed later
For the first runtime, read-focused workflow inspection is enough.
________________


11. GET /workflows/{workflow_id}
Purpose
Retrieve current workflow state.
Response fields
                                                   * workflow_id
                                                   * conversation_id
                                                   * task_id
                                                   * current status
                                                   * active owner/service
                                                   * memory lookup status
                                                   * verification status
                                                   * admission status
                                                   * timestamps
Example response:
{
  "workflow_id": "wf.100001",
  "conversation_id": "conv.100001",
  "task_id": "t.climate.001",
  "status": "verification_pending",
  "active_owner": "ag.verification.01",
  "memory_lookup_status": "miss",
  "verification_status": "pending",
  "admission_status": "not_started"
}

________________
12. GET /workflows/{workflow_id}/trace
Purpose
Retrieve full workflow execution trace.
Response
Should include:
                                                   * ordered bundle history
                                                   * message history summary
                                                   * state transitions
                                                   * agent/service participants
                                                   * errors if any
This is essential for debugging and operator inspection.
________________


13. GET /workflows/{workflow_id}/result
Purpose
Retrieve the latest semantic result for a workflow.
Response modes
Should support:
                                                   * semantic_bundle
                                                   * aasl
                                                   * summary
                                                   * full
This lets callers retrieve either:
                                                   * native semantic content
                                                   * or a human-oriented view
________________


14. Semantic Query API
This is the externalized interface to the query engine.
Its responsibilities are:
                                                   * object lookup
                                                   * claim retrieval
                                                   * relationship traversal
                                                   * verification-aware retrieval
                                                   * document and bundle retrieval
                                                   * semantic filtering
The first runtime should expose:
14.1 Get Object by ID
14.2 Search Objects
14.3 Get Claim Bundle
14.4 Traverse Related Objects
________________


15. GET /semantic/objects/{object_id}
Purpose
Retrieve one semantic object by ID.
Response
Should return:
                                                   * object fields
                                                   * object type
                                                   * lifecycle state
                                                   * bundle/document membership
                                                   * verification/canonical state
                                                   * references summary
This is the basic semantic inspection API.
________________


16. GET /semantic/claims/{claim_id}/bundle
Purpose
Retrieve a full claim-centered semantic bundle.
Response
Should include:
                                                   * CLM
                                                   * attached CNF
                                                   * attached PRV
                                                   * attached VRF
                                                   * related ACT if known
                                                   * document/bundle context
This is one of the most important APIs because claims are the primary knowledge unit for reuse.
________________


17. POST /semantic/query
Purpose
Run structured semantic queries.
Request should support filters like:
                                                   * object type
                                                   * field equality
                                                   * field range
                                                   * verification state
                                                   * canonical state
                                                   * document ID
                                                   * bundle ID
                                                   * target object
                                                   * claim type
Example request:
{
  "object_type": "CLM",
  "filters": {
    "type": "correlation",
    "verification_state": "verified",
    "target_dataset": "ds.climate.44"
  },
  "result_shape": "bundle_summary"
}
Response
Returns matching semantic objects or bundles in the requested result shape.
________________


18. GET /semantic/objects/{object_id}/related
Purpose
Traverse inbound and outbound semantic relationships.
Query parameters
                                                   * direction: inbound / outbound / both
                                                   * relationship_kind
                                                   * depth
                                                   * include_attachments
This endpoint gives graph-style exploration to external tooling and operator UIs.
________________


19. Memory API
The Memory API exposes semantic memory behavior explicitly.
Its responsibilities are:
                                                   * lookup reusable semantic bundles
                                                   * inspect duplicate/equivalence relationships
                                                   * retrieve latest verified reusable knowledge
                                                   * inspect admission decisions
The first runtime should expose:
19.1 Lookup Reusable Bundle
19.2 Get Latest Verified for Target
19.3 Inspect Duplicate / Equivalence
19.4 Inspect Admission Result
________________


20. POST /memory/lookup
Purpose
Check whether reusable semantic knowledge already exists.
Request
May include:
                                                   * target object ID
                                                   * task op
                                                   * candidate semantic signature
                                                   * canonical hash if known
                                                   * optional query constraints
Example:
{
  "task_op": "analyze",
  "target_id": "ds.climate.44",
  "preferred_claim_type": "correlation"
}
Response
Returns:
                                                   * hit / miss / partial
                                                   * matched bundle IDs
                                                   * confidence/trust summary
                                                   * latest verified reusable result if found
This is the external API analog of the internal memory lookup message.
________________


21. GET /memory/targets/{target_id}/latest-verified
Purpose
Retrieve the latest trusted reusable semantic knowledge for a target.
Response
Should include:
                                                   * latest claim bundle(s)
                                                   * verification state
                                                   * storage tier
                                                   * provenance summary
                                                   * supersession information if any
This endpoint is central for semantic reuse.
________________


22. GET /memory/equivalence/{canonical_hash}
Purpose
Inspect duplicate/equivalent artifacts tied to a canonical hash.
Response
Returns:
                                                   * canonical representative
                                                   * equivalent object/bundle IDs
                                                   * current preferred version
                                                   * conflict/supersession notes
This is important for debugging memory reuse and deduplication behavior.
________________


23. Export API
The Export API is responsible for turning runtime or stored semantic artifacts back into durable representations.
Its responsibilities are:
                                                   * export canonical .aas
                                                   * export JSON
                                                   * export human-readable summaries
                                                   * export bundle payloads
The first runtime should expose:
23.1 Export Bundle
23.2 Export Document
23.3 Export Object Bundle
23.4 Export Summary
________________


24. GET /export/bundles/{bundle_id}
Purpose
Export a stored semantic bundle.
Query parameters
                                                   * format=aasl|json|summary
                                                   * optional include_context=true|false
Response
Returns the bundle in the requested format.
This is critical for interoperability, operator review, and debugging.
________________


25. GET /export/documents/{document_id}
Purpose
Export a document artifact in canonical form.
Response
Should support:
                                                   * canonical .aas
                                                   * .aas.json
                                                   * optional wrapper-safe text format
This endpoint uses the file infrastructure and document builder.
________________


26. Operator / Inspection API
The Operator API supports runtime inspection and administrative observability.
Its responsibilities are:
                                                   * inspect runtime health
                                                   * inspect unresolved references
                                                   * inspect quarantined artifacts
                                                   * inspect verification failures
                                                   * inspect storage tier contents
                                                   * inspect workflow backlogs
The first runtime should expose:
26.1 Runtime Health
26.2 Queue / Workload Status
26.3 Quarantine Inspection
26.4 Verification Failure Inspection
26.5 Storage Tier Summary
________________


27. GET /ops/runtime/health
Purpose
Return runtime system health summary.
Should include:
                                                   * service availability
                                                   * bundle counts by state
                                                   * workflow counts by state
                                                   * unresolved reference count
                                                   * verification backlog count
                                                   * memory hit rate
                                                   * storage write health
This endpoint is for operator dashboards and runtime monitoring.
________________


28. GET /ops/quarantine
Purpose
Inspect quarantined bundles and objects.
Response
Should include:
                                                   * bundle IDs
                                                   * quarantine reasons
                                                   * source workflow/task
                                                   * admission state
                                                   * related diagnostics
This is important for debugging trust and admission failures.
________________


29. GET /ops/verification/failures
Purpose
Inspect verification failures or disputes.
Response
Should include:
                                                   * affected claims/bundles
                                                   * verification status
                                                   * verifier ID
                                                   * dispute reasons
                                                   * related workflow IDs
This helps operators understand where semantic trust is breaking down.
________________


30. Internal Service APIs
In addition to external APIs, the first runtime should define internal service APIs between:
                                                   * ingress service
                                                   * coordinator service
                                                   * query service
                                                   * memory service
                                                   * storage service
These internal APIs should mirror the same semantic model but may be narrower and more operationally optimized.
Key internal API groups:
Coordinator Internal API
                                                   * create workflow
                                                   * record state transition
                                                   * assign bundle
                                                   * finalize workflow
Memory Internal API
                                                   * lookup reusable bundle
                                                   * admit verified bundle
                                                   * fetch canonical representative
Storage Internal API
                                                   * persist bundle
                                                   * persist object set
                                                   * reconstruct bundle
                                                   * query by index
Query Internal API
                                                   * get object neighborhood
                                                   * get claim attachment set
                                                   * search semantic corpus
These APIs should still operate on bundle and AASL contracts, even if not directly exposed externally.
________________


31. API Versioning
Every API family should be versioned explicitly.
Recommended path style:
                                                   * /v1/ingress/...
                                                   * /v1/workflows/...
                                                   * /v1/semantic/...
                                                   * /v1/memory/...
                                                   * /v1/export/...
                                                   * /v1/ops/...
And every response should also declare:
                                                   * aasl_version
                                                   * ontology_version
                                                   * protocol_version where relevant
This keeps the external surface aligned with the governed language ecosystem.
________________


32. API Result Modes
Many APIs should support multiple result modes.
Recommended modes:
semantic_bundle
Returns native semantic structures.
aasl
Returns canonical AASL text.
json
Returns structured JSON serialization.
summary
Returns reduced human-readable summaries.
full
Returns semantic bundle plus metadata and diagnostics.
This is important because different consumers need different levels of fidelity.
________________


33. API Error Model
APIs must return structured errors, not ad hoc strings.
Each error should include:
                                                   * error_code
                                                   * error_category
                                                   * message
                                                   * related_workflow_id
                                                   * related_bundle_id
                                                   * retry_allowed
                                                   * optional diagnostics
Core categories:
                                                   * ingress error
                                                   * parse error
                                                   * validation error
                                                   * execution error
                                                   * verification error
                                                   * admission error
                                                   * query error
                                                   * export error
                                                   * operator permission error
This aligns the API layer with the runtime’s semantic failure model.
________________


34. API Authentication and Authorization
Even in the first runtime, the API layer should be designed to support scoped access.
Minimum distinctions should be anticipated for:
                                                   * public task submission
                                                   * internal service calls
                                                   * operator inspection
                                                   * trusted export
                                                   * memory inspection
                                                   * quarantine inspection
Even if first implementation uses a simple auth mechanism, the contract layer should be designed so that role-based access can be enforced later without changing endpoint semantics.
________________


35. API Contracts in the Repo
The exact API contracts should live in:
schemas/api/
Recommended structure:
schemas/api/
├── ingress/
├── workflows/
├── semantic/
├── memory/
├── export/
└── ops/
These should define:
                                                   * request schemas
                                                   * response schemas
                                                   * error schemas
                                                   * result modes
                                                   * versioning expectations
Implementation adapters should live in the relevant service apps/modules.
________________


36. API-to-Service Mapping
A clear first-runtime mapping should be:
API Gateway routes to:
                                                   * Ingress Service for /ingress
                                                   * Coordinator/Execution view for /workflows
                                                   * Query Service for /semantic
                                                   * Memory Service for /memory
                                                   * Export layer for /export
                                                   * Operator Console/ops adapters for /ops
This keeps the gateway thin and the semantic services authoritative.
________________


37. First Complete User-Level API Flow
A typical external flow should look like this:
                                                   1. POST /v1/ingress/tasks
                                                   2. receive workflow_id
                                                   3. GET /v1/workflows/{workflow_id}
                                                   4. if completed, call:
                                                   * GET /v1/workflows/{workflow_id}/result?mode=summary
                                                   * or GET /v1/workflows/{workflow_id}/result?mode=semantic_bundle
                                                   5. optionally inspect reusable memory via:
                                                   * POST /v1/memory/lookup
                                                   6. optionally export final semantic result via:
                                                   * GET /v1/export/bundles/{bundle_id}?format=aasl
That is the first full external operating loop.
________________


38. What This API Layer Enables
If implemented correctly, this API layer enables:
                                                   * external task submission
                                                   * semantic preview and validation
                                                   * workflow lifecycle inspection
                                                   * semantic retrieval by object, claim, and relationship
                                                   * memory-first reuse APIs
                                                   * canonical export
                                                   * operator-grade runtime inspection
This turns the first runtime from an internal service mesh into an actual callable platform.
________________


39. Final Summary
The first runtime should expose a versioned API contract layer organized into six families:
                                                   * Ingress API
                                                   * Workflow API
                                                   * Semantic Query API
                                                   * Memory API
                                                   * Export API
                                                   * Operator / Inspection API
These APIs should accept conventional external input formats where needed, but all meaningful runtime operations must resolve to AASL-native bundle and object semantics. Responses should expose semantic, validation, canonicalization, verification, and admission state explicitly, with support for multiple result modes such as semantic_bundle, aasl, json, and summary.
This API layer is the external and internal callable surface of the first AASL-native Atrahasis runtime.
________________


The next thing we should work on is:
the exact end-to-end implementation sequence for building the first runtime
That means defining, in implementation order:
                                                   * what gets built first
                                                   * what each milestone produces
                                                   * dependency order between parser, runtime, storage, agents, and APIs
                                                   * what must exist before the next subsystem can be added
                                                   * what the first runnable milestone should be
That is the cleanest next step because the architecture is now implementation-ready, and the remaining question is build order.
Exact End-to-End Implementation Sequence for Building the First Runtime
At this point, the architecture is no longer hypothetical. The remaining question is execution order.
The first AASL-native Atrahasis runtime should not be built by trying to implement every subsystem at once. Even though the full architecture is defined, the implementation still needs a strict dependency-aware sequence so that each layer produces stable inputs for the next.
This sequence answers:
What do we build first, what depends on it, what is the first runnable milestone, and how do we move from zero code to a complete working AASL-native runtime without architectural drift?
The implementation order below is designed so that:
                                                   * every step has a clear deliverable
                                                   * every step creates a reusable foundation for the next
                                                   * every milestone proves a real capability
                                                   * no critical subsystem is built on unstable contracts
                                                   * the first end-to-end semantic loop appears as early as possible without cheating the architecture
________________


1. Implementation Principle
The build order must follow the semantic dependency chain, not UI preference or convenience.
That means the true order is:
                                                   1. language core
                                                   2. parsing and validation
                                                   3. canonicalization
                                                   4. runtime object model
                                                   5. storage contracts
                                                   6. message contracts
                                                   7. query and memory primitives
                                                   8. coordinator and agent execution
                                                   9. verification loop
                                                   10. external APIs and operator tooling
This is the only order that keeps the system genuinely AASL-native.
If you start with UI or APIs first, you will almost certainly reintroduce ad hoc JSON semantics and architectural inconsistency.
________________


2. Global Milestone Structure
The full first-runtime implementation should be divided into these major milestones:
                                                   1. Milestone 0 — Repo and contract scaffolding
                                                   2. Milestone 1 — AASL core language implementation
                                                   3. Milestone 2 — Runtime object system
                                                   4. Milestone 3 — Storage and bundle persistence
                                                   5. Milestone 4 — AACP + AASL internal messaging
                                                   6. Milestone 5 — Query + memory-first retrieval
                                                   7. Milestone 6 — Coordinator and first agent loop
                                                   8. Milestone 7 — Verification and trusted admission
                                                   9. Milestone 8 — External APIs
                                                   10. Milestone 9 — Operator inspection and full end-to-end hardening
Each milestone should be fully completed before the next one is considered stable enough to build on.
________________


3. Milestone 0 — Repo and Contract Scaffolding
This milestone creates the implementation skeleton.
Goal
Set up the repo so all later work lands in the correct boundaries and contracts are authoritative from day one.
Build now
                                                   * monorepo structure
                                                   * package boundaries
                                                   * service directories
                                                   * schema directories
                                                   * test directories
                                                   * linting/formatting/build tooling
                                                   * dependency rules
                                                   * shared version constants
Deliverables
                                                   * working monorepo
                                                   * empty but valid package structure
                                                   * placeholder packages:
                                                   * aasl-core
                                                   * aasl-parser
                                                   * aasl-validator
                                                   * aasl-canonicalizer
                                                   * aasl-runtime
                                                   * aasl-storage-contracts
                                                   * aacp-contracts
                                                   * agent-contracts
                                                   * schema folders for:
                                                   * AASL
                                                   * storage
                                                   * API
                                                   * AACP
                                                   * test harness with fixture loading
Why this first
Because all later implementation must land in stable module boundaries. If this is not done first, the codebase will sprawl.
________________


4. Milestone 1 — AASL Core Language Implementation
This is the first true language milestone.
Goal
Make AASL parseable, validatable, and canonicalizable in code.
Build now
4.1 aasl-core
                                                   * object type definitions
                                                   * field definitions
                                                   * section definitions
                                                   * base enums
                                                   * version metadata models
4.2 aasl-parser
                                                   * lexer
                                                   * parser
                                                   * CST/AST
                                                   * diagnostics
                                                   * basic symbol table
                                                   * tolerant and strict parse modes
4.3 aasl-validator
                                                   * structural rules
                                                   * template rules
                                                   * type/value rules
                                                   * ontology rules
                                                   * reference rules
                                                   * document rules
4.4 aasl-canonicalizer
                                                   * canonical field ordering
                                                   * canonical slot normalization
                                                   * ID normalization
                                                   * timestamp normalization
                                                   * numeric normalization
                                                   * canonical emission order
Deliverables
                                                   * parse .aas
                                                   * validate .aas
                                                   * canonicalize .aas
                                                   * emit canonical .aas
                                                   * conformance tests for parser/validator/canonicalizer
                                                   * canonical fixtures in testdata/
First proof
You can take a hand-written or compiled AASL file and prove:
                                                   * it parses
                                                   * it validates
                                                   * it canonicalizes deterministically
Why before runtime
Because runtime, storage, messaging, and agents all depend on a stable language implementation.
________________


5. Milestone 2 — Runtime Object System
Once the language exists in code, it must become live semantic state.
Goal
Turn parsed AASL into active runtime objects with references and state.
Build now
5.1 aasl-runtime
                                                   * runtime object model
                                                   * object registry
                                                   * type registry
                                                   * document registry
                                                   * reference resolver
                                                   * unresolved reference tracking
                                                   * lifecycle state tracking
5.2 hydration pipeline
                                                   * parser output → runtime objects
                                                   * canonicalized document → runtime graph
5.3 state model
                                                   * parsed
                                                   * validated
                                                   * canonical
                                                   * verified
                                                   * mutable/immutable
                                                   * dirty/clean
Deliverables
                                                   * load canonical AASL into runtime
                                                   * retrieve by ID/type
                                                   * traverse references
                                                   * reconstruct object neighborhoods
                                                   * runtime tests for object identity, relationships, and state
First proof
You can load a full AASL bundle and inspect it as semantic runtime state rather than raw text.
Why before storage
Because storage schema and query behavior must be based on the true runtime object model.
________________


6. Milestone 3 — Storage and Bundle Persistence
Now that bundles and objects can exist in runtime, they need persistence.
Goal
Store semantic bundles durably and retrieve them back into runtime.
Build now
6.1 aasl-storage-contracts
                                                   * bundle interfaces
                                                   * document persistence interfaces
                                                   * object persistence interfaces
                                                   * reference persistence interfaces
                                                   * retrieval interfaces
6.2 storage-service
                                                   * bundle store
                                                   * object store
                                                   * reference store
                                                   * verification store skeleton
                                                   * provenance store skeleton
                                                   * execution store
                                                   * canonical hash index
                                                   * bundle reconstruction logic
6.3 file integration
                                                   * persist canonical .aas
                                                   * retrieve canonical .aas
                                                   * rehydrate runtime from persisted bundle
Deliverables
                                                   * store bundle
                                                   * store objects
                                                   * store references
                                                   * reconstruct bundle by bundle_id
                                                   * retrieve object by object_id
                                                   * persist execution state minimally
First proof
You can submit a canonical bundle, persist it, shut down, restart, and reconstruct the same semantic state.
Why before agents
