Because agents must have somewhere real to write results and memory must exist before memory-first logic can be meaningful.
________________


7. Milestone 4 — AACP + AASL Internal Messaging
Now internal communication needs to exist in code.
Goal
Implement the exact runtime message contracts already defined.
Build now
7.1 aacp-contracts
                                                   * header models
                                                   * bundle wrapper models
                                                   * message class models
                                                   * validation for message/header/payload consistency
7.2 messaging transport library
                                                   * message serialization/deserialization
                                                   * transport adapters
                                                   * correlation/workflow propagation
                                                   * parent-child message tracing
7.3 first runtime message families
                                                   * task_submission
                                                   * task_assignment
                                                   * task_result
                                                   * verification_request
                                                   * verification_result
                                                   * memory_lookup_request
                                                   * memory_lookup_result
                                                   * memory_admission_request
                                                   * memory_admission_result
                                                   * state_update
                                                   * error_report
Deliverables
                                                   * message creation library
                                                   * message validation library
                                                   * send/receive path between test services
                                                   * workflow trace linkage across messages
First proof
Two services can exchange a valid AACP message carrying a real AASL bundle and reconstruct the same semantic state.
Why before coordinator
Because coordinator and agents must speak a stable wire contract before orchestration logic is built.
________________


8. Milestone 5 — Query + Memory-First Retrieval
Now that runtime objects, storage, and internal messages exist, semantic retrieval can become operational.
Goal
Make the system capable of asking, “Do we already know this?”
Build now
8.1 aasl-query
                                                   * ID lookup
                                                   * type lookup
                                                   * field filtering
                                                   * relationship traversal
                                                   * claim bundle retrieval
                                                   * verification attachment retrieval
8.2 memory-service
                                                   * semantic lookup by target
                                                   * canonical hash lookup
                                                   * bundle reuse lookup
                                                   * latest verified result lookup
                                                   * duplicate/equivalence detection
                                                   * hit/miss result generation
8.3 storage indexes
                                                   * bundle by task/target
                                                   * object by type
                                                   * canonical hash lookup
                                                   * verification status lookup
Deliverables
                                                   * runtime query interface
                                                   * storage-backed retrieval
                                                   * memory lookup request/result flow
                                                   * reusable bundle retrieval
First proof
Given a semantic target, the system can retrieve previously stored verified knowledge instead of forcing recomputation.
Why before coordinator loop
Because coordinator behavior is defined around memory-first execution.
________________


9. Milestone 6 — Coordinator and First Agent Loop
Now the system can begin performing work.
Goal
Implement the first complete unverified execution path:
ingress → coordinator → research/analysis → result bundle.
Build now
9.1 coordinator-service
                                                   * workflow creation
                                                   * task routing
                                                   * memory lookup invocation
                                                   * assignment generation
                                                   * result collection
                                                   * workflow state transitions
9.2 agent-service
Implement the first three agent roles:
                                                   * Coordinator contract enforcement
                                                   * Research Agent
                                                   * Analysis Agent
9.3 agent-contracts
                                                   * role interfaces
                                                   * input bundle validation
                                                   * output bundle generation
                                                   * lifecycle and failure semantics
9.4 ingress-service
                                                   * submit raw input
                                                   * compile to AASL task bundle
                                                   * hand off to coordinator
Deliverables
                                                   * end-to-end task execution without verification
                                                   * real task_submission → memory_lookup_request → miss → task_assignment → task_result
                                                   * result bundle persistence in draft/canonical state
First proof
A user can submit a task and receive a real AASL result bundle generated by the runtime.
Why before verification
Because the system must generate candidate semantic knowledge before it can verify it.
________________


10. Milestone 7 — Verification and Trusted Admission
Now the system can become trustworthy rather than merely productive.
Goal
Close the full semantic loop:
candidate result → verification → memory admission → reusable trusted knowledge.
Build now
10.1 verification-service
                                                   * verification request handling
                                                   * candidate bundle inspection
                                                   * claim/evidence comparison
                                                   * VRF emission
                                                   * dispute/reject paths
10.2 expand memory-service
                                                   * admission decision logic
                                                   * verified tier promotion
                                                   * duplicate reuse
                                                   * supersession/conflict handling basics
10.3 expand storage
                                                   * verification store
                                                   * tier state tracking
                                                   * admission state tracking
                                                   * latest verified representative selection
Deliverables
                                                   * verification_request / verification_result
                                                   * memory_admission_request / memory_admission_result
                                                   * verified bundle persistence
                                                   * trusted/verified tier
                                                   * basic conflict and duplicate handling
First proof
A result can be verified and committed to semantic memory as trusted reusable knowledge.
Critical proof
A second equivalent task should now hit memory and return the stored verified result rather than recomputing it.
This is the single most important milestone in the whole first runtime.
________________


11. Milestone 8 — External APIs
Only after the full semantic loop works internally should the external surface be formalized.
Goal
Expose the runtime as a callable system.
Build now
11.1 api-gateway
                                                   * route external API calls
                                                   * auth scaffolding
                                                   * request normalization
                                                   * response envelope shaping
11.2 implement API families
                                                   * Ingress API
                                                   * Workflow API
                                                   * Semantic Query API
                                                   * Memory API
                                                   * Export API
                                                   * Operator API basics
11.3 result shaping
                                                   * semantic_bundle
                                                   * aasl
                                                   * json
                                                   * summary
Deliverables
                                                   * submit task over API
                                                   * inspect workflow over API
                                                   * retrieve result over API
                                                   * query semantic object over API
                                                   * check reusable memory over API
                                                   * export .aas over API
First proof
The system is now a callable platform, not just internal services.
Why after internal loop
Because APIs should expose working semantic capabilities, not drive architecture prematurely.
________________


12. Milestone 9 — Operator Inspection and Full End-to-End Hardening
Now the runtime works. The final first-runtime milestone is observability, hardening, and operational control.
Goal
Make the runtime inspectable, debuggable, and stable enough for repeated use.
Build now
12.1 operator console / runtime dev shell
                                                   * workflow trace view
                                                   * bundle inspection
                                                   * object inspection
                                                   * verification failure view
                                                   * quarantine view
                                                   * memory hit/miss dashboard
12.2 observability
                                                   * task metrics
                                                   * bundle metrics
                                                   * memory hit rate
                                                   * verification rate
                                                   * latency metrics
                                                   * error rate metrics
12.3 hardening
                                                   * replayable test scenarios
                                                   * conformance tests for the runtime loop
                                                   * storage recovery tests
                                                   * failure injection tests
                                                   * retry policy tests
Deliverables
                                                   * operator visibility into all major runtime states
                                                   * reproducible e2e scenarios
                                                   * local dev environment with seeded fixtures
                                                   * stable first-runtime demo
Final proof
The whole runtime can be demonstrated, debugged, and exercised repeatedly with confidence.
________________


13. The First Runnable Milestone
The first milestone that should be considered truly “runnable” is not Milestone 1.
The first meaningful runnable milestone is:
Milestone 6
because that is the first point where:
                                                   * ingress exists
                                                   * coordinator exists
                                                   * agents exist
                                                   * tasks actually run
However, the first architecturally complete runnable milestone is:
Milestone 7
because that is the first point where:
                                                   * knowledge can be produced
                                                   * knowledge can be verified
                                                   * knowledge can be stored
                                                   * knowledge can be reused
Milestone 7 is the first moment Atrahasis becomes cumulative semantic intelligence rather than a task pipeline.
________________


14. Critical Dependency Order
The dependency order must remain strict:
Must exist before agents
                                                   * AASL core
                                                   * parser
                                                   * validator
                                                   * canonicalizer
                                                   * runtime object model
                                                   * message contracts
Must exist before memory-first logic
                                                   * storage schema
                                                   * query engine
                                                   * canonical hash persistence
Must exist before verified memory
                                                   * verification service
                                                   * admission logic
                                                   * verified tier persistence
Must exist before public APIs
                                                   * stable internal workflow loop
                                                   * stable message contracts
                                                   * stable storage and query paths
Any deviation from this order risks introducing nonsemantic shortcuts that will have to be torn out later.
________________


15. Recommended Build Teams by Milestone
If multiple streams of work are happening in parallel, they should still respect milestone boundaries.
Milestones 0–1
Language implementation team:
                                                   * core
                                                   * parser
                                                   * validator
                                                   * canonicalizer
Milestones 2–3
Semantic infrastructure team:
                                                   * runtime
                                                   * storage contracts
                                                   * persistence
                                                   * bundle model
Milestones 4–5
Execution substrate team:
                                                   * AACP messaging
                                                   * query engine
                                                   * memory service
Milestones 6–7
Runtime orchestration team:
                                                   * ingress
                                                   * coordinator
                                                   * agents
                                                   * verification
                                                   * admission
Milestones 8–9
Platform and operations team:
                                                   * APIs
                                                   * operator console
                                                   * observability
                                                   * hardening
This keeps implementation parallelizable without violating dependency integrity.
________________


16. What Each Milestone Produces
To make the sequence concrete:
Milestone 0 produces
A buildable, testable repo skeleton.
Milestone 1 produces
A real language implementation.
Milestone 2 produces
A live semantic runtime graph.
Milestone 3 produces
Durable semantic persistence.
Milestone 4 produces
Semantic internal communication.
Milestone 5 produces
Memory-first retrieval capability.
Milestone 6 produces
Executable semantic agent workflows.
Milestone 7 produces
Verified reusable knowledge.
Milestone 8 produces
A callable runtime platform.
Milestone 9 produces
An operable and inspectable runtime system.
This is the shortest sequence that still preserves the full architecture.
________________


17. The Single Most Important Acceptance Test
The one end-to-end acceptance test that should be used to judge success of the first runtime is this:
                                                   1. Submit a natural-language task.
                                                   2. Compile it into AASL.
                                                   3. Execute it through coordinator + agents.
                                                   4. Produce a candidate semantic result.
                                                   5. Verify that result.
                                                   6. Store the verified bundle.
                                                   7. Submit a semantically equivalent second task.
                                                   8. Confirm the system reuses stored semantic knowledge instead of recomputing.
If this works, then the entire thesis of AASL-native Atrahasis has been proven.
________________


18. Final Summary
The exact end-to-end implementation sequence for the first runtime should be:
                                                   1. Repo and contract scaffolding
                                                   2. AASL core language implementation
                                                   3. Runtime object system
                                                   4. Storage and bundle persistence
                                                   5. AACP + AASL internal messaging
                                                   6. Query + memory-first retrieval
                                                   7. Coordinator and first agent loop
                                                   8. Verification and trusted admission
                                                   9. External APIs
                                                   10. Operator inspection and hardening
The first meaningful runnable system appears at Milestone 6.
The first architecturally complete AASL-native Atrahasis runtime appears at Milestone 7.
That is the exact build order that preserves the architecture and gets to a real semantic intelligence loop as directly as possible.
________________

                                                   * repo creation tasks

                                                   * acceptance criteria
That is the right next step because the sequence is now defined, and the next practical move is to convert the first implementation phase into an executable build plan.
Below is the full implementation checklist and deliverable list for all milestones of the first AASL-native Atrahasis runtime.
This is written as an execution plan, not just an architecture summary. Each milestone includes:
                                                   * objective
                                                   * concrete implementation checklist
                                                   * deliverables
                                                   * acceptance criteria
                                                   * dependency notes

                                                   * PROVENANCE
                                                   * VERIFICATION
                                                   * FOOTER
                                                   * Define common field names

                                                   * Define version constants
aasl-parser
                                                   * Implement source manager
                                                   * Implement lexer
                                                   * Implement token model
                                                   * Implement parser grammar

                                                   * Implement AST output

                                                   * Implement diagnostics model

                                                   * Implement tolerant mode

                                                   * Implement field/value parsing

                                                   * Implement unresolved reference collection
aasl-validator
                                                   * Implement structural validation

Deliverables

                                                   * Validator catches required rule violations

Deliverables

Acceptance criteria

                                                   * Send/receive between test services
                                                   * Message round-trip integrity
                                                   * Workflow trace continuity across messages
Deliverables
                                                   * Message contract library
                                                   * Internal transport implementation
                                                   * Validated AACP + AASL messages between services
Acceptance criteria
                                                   * Two services can exchange a valid semantic message
                                                   * Received payload reconstructs the same bundle semantics
                                                   * Workflow/message lineage remains intact across exchanges
Dependency notes
Coordinator, agents, and verification should not be implemented before this is stable.

Cross-Milestone Acceptance Test
The single most important acceptance test across all milestones is:
                                                   1. Submit a natural-language task.
                                                   2. Compile it into AASL.
                                                   3. Create workflow and task bundle.
                                                   4. Perform memory lookup.
                                                   5. On miss, dispatch to Research and Analysis agents.
                                                   6. Produce candidate semantic claim bundle.
                                                   7. Verify the bundle.
                                                   8. Admit verified bundle into trusted memory.
                                                   9. Submit an equivalent second task.
                                                   10. Confirm the second task reuses trusted semantic memory instead of recomputing.
If this works, the first AASL-native Atrahasis runtime is proven.

Final Note
At this point, the entire AASL + Atrahasis runtime architecture is fully specified down to implementation tasks.
The only remaining thing before real development begins is creating:
1. A full system architecture diagram
2. A single master design document
that consolidates everything we've built in this conversation into one canonical spec.
If you'd like, I can generate the Atrahasis AASL Runtime Master Specification next.
The one hidden architectural risk is:
semantic drift between the formal system and the actual execution system
In plain terms:
You designed AASL as the true internal language, but when teams actually implement systems like this, they almost always let the runtime slowly fall back to:
                                                   * raw strings
                                                   * ad hoc JSON fields
                                                   * undocumented side-channel metadata
                                                   * implicit assumptions inside agent prompts
                                                   * special-case service logic that is not represented in the canonical semantic model
Once that happens, the architecture still looks AASL-native on paper, but the real system is no longer governed by AASL. It becomes a hybrid mess where:
                                                   * some truth lives in AASL
                                                   * some truth lives in prompts
                                                   * some truth lives in service code
                                                   * some truth lives in DB-only fields
                                                   * some truth lives in UI assumptions
That is the failure mode.
________________


Why this is the most dangerous risk
Because it does not look like a failure at first.
The system still appears to work.
Tasks run.
Agents respond.
Bundles are stored.
APIs return results.
But over time:
                                                   * verification becomes less reliable because some meaning is outside AASL
                                                   * deduplication becomes weaker because equivalent semantics are represented differently in hidden layers
                                                   * memory reuse becomes inconsistent because matching depends on undocumented runtime logic
                                                   * debugging becomes brutal because the semantic truth is split across multiple representations
                                                   * federation becomes fragile because remote nodes only see the AASL subset, not the hidden execution assumptions
This is how most “agent systems” quietly fail architecturally.
They do not fail because the idea is bad.
They fail because the implementation leaks meaning outside the formal substrate.
________________


What it looks like in practice
Here is how this usually happens.
1. Prompt logic becomes a hidden ontology
A Research Agent is supposed to output EVD, PRV, and maybe draft CLM.
But then someone adds a prompt instruction like:
“If the source seems highly trustworthy, prefer asserting the strongest likely causal relationship.”
That instruction changes semantic behavior, but it is not represented as:
                                                   * a formal policy object
                                                   * a constraint object
                                                   * a reasoning mode object
                                                   * or any AASL artifact
Now the real semantics live partly in the prompt.
That is drift.
________________


2. JSON fields appear that AASL does not model
A service starts storing fields like:
                                                   * confidence_reasoning_trace
                                                   * trust_boost
                                                   * priority_override
                                                   * semantic_similarity_score
                                                   * agent_override_mode
These fields are operationally important, but they are not modeled in AASL.
Now decisions are being made from metadata outside the formal semantic system.
That is drift.
________________


3. Coordinator logic becomes “magic”
The Coordinator is supposed to route based on:
                                                   * task
                                                   * constraints
                                                   * memory state
                                                   * verification state
But later developers add special routing rules directly in code like:
                                                   * “if task came from premium user, skip research”
                                                   * “if claim type is correlation and source is dataset X, route to fast path”
                                                   * “if prior verification is recent, bypass verification”
If those decisions are not formally represented in semantic policy/state objects, then the runtime truth is no longer fully inside AASL.
That is drift.
________________


4. Memory admission starts depending on hidden heuristics
Your Memory Agent is supposed to admit based on:
                                                   * validation
                                                   * canonicalization
                                                   * verification
                                                   * policy
But then people add hidden checks such as:
                                                   * string similarity
                                                   * undocumented trust scores
                                                   * service-local flags
                                                   * hand-coded exceptions
Now memory behavior cannot be fully explained from stored AASL artifacts.
That is drift.
________________


5. Verification compares artifacts using noncanonical side logic
If verification starts using:
                                                   * raw model text
                                                   * prompt-specific explanations
                                                   * undocumented evaluator scores
instead of primarily:
                                                   * canonical semantic objects
                                                   * evidence objects
                                                   * provenance objects
                                                   * explicit verification records
then trust is no longer anchored to the formal semantic substrate.
That is drift.
________________


Why almost every agent system falls into this trap
Because it is extremely tempting.
A formal system like AASL feels strict.
Engineers under delivery pressure will naturally do things like:
                                                   * “just add one field”
                                                   * “just pass this hidden flag”
                                                   * “just keep this reasoning note outside the schema”
                                                   * “just handle this one case in code”
                                                   * “just add this prompt convention”
Each shortcut seems harmless.
But every shortcut moves meaning out of the formal language and into informal execution layers.
Eventually the real system is no longer:
AASL → runtime → verification → memory
It becomes:
AASL + prompts + hidden metadata + service heuristics + DB hacks
At that point, the semantic architecture is mostly theater.
________________


Why this risk is especially serious for your design
Your architecture depends on five things being true:
                                                   1. canonicalization must be authoritative
                                                   2. verification must compare formal semantics
                                                   3. memory reuse must depend on canonical semantic identity
                                                   4. federation must exchange the full meaning
                                                   5. governance must evolve the formal system, not hidden behavior
If semantic drift occurs, all five break.
That means the exact features that make AASL valuable are the same features most vulnerable to erosion.
________________


The core symptom to watch for
The warning sign is this:
Any operationally important fact that affects routing, trust, storage, reuse, or interpretation but is not representable in AASL is a structural defect.
That is the test.
Ask of every behavior:
                                                   * Can this be represented as AASL?
                                                   * Can it be validated?
                                                   * Can it be stored?
                                                   * Can it be inspected?
                                                   * Can it be federated?
                                                   * Can it be governed?
If the answer is no, then you are creating semantic drift.
________________


The specific principle that prevents it
You need one hard architectural law:
No hidden semantics rule
Any data that affects:
                                                   * agent behavior
                                                   * workflow routing
                                                   * verification outcome
                                                   * memory admission
                                                   * semantic identity
                                                   * trust tier
                                                   * federation behavior
must exist as one of the following:
                                                   1. an AASL object
                                                   2. a formally defined AASL-adjacent contract field
                                                   3. a governed policy object linked into the semantic system
If it affects the system and is not formally modeled, it is not allowed.
That one rule will save the architecture.
________________


What to do concretely
You should enforce this in implementation with these safeguards.
1. Semantic closure review
Before any new runtime feature is added, require a review question:
Where does this meaning live formally?
If the answer is “in code” or “in the prompt,” that is a red flag.
________________


2. Prompts must be semantically bounded
Prompts can exist, but they must not define hidden business logic.
Prompts should be constrained to:
                                                   * transformation guidance
                                                   * extraction assistance
                                                   * language generation support
They should not be the sole location of:
                                                   * trust policy
                                                   * routing logic
                                                   * ontology meaning
                                                   * memory admission rules
                                                   * verification standards
________________


3. Every important runtime decision should emit semantic trace
If a coordinator routes a task, there should be a formal trace object or state record.
If memory rejects a bundle, there should be a formal admission result.
If verification disputes a claim, there should be a formal dispute artifact.
No invisible decision paths.
________________


4. Ban ungoverned side fields
Do not let teams add arbitrary JSON metadata fields that influence behavior unless those fields are:
                                                   * in a formal contract
                                                   * reviewed
                                                   * versioned
                                                   * documented
                                                   * ideally representable in AASL or a governed adjacent schema
________________


5. Make operator tooling expose hidden-state pressure
Your inspection tools should show:
                                                   * why a task was routed
                                                   * why memory admitted or rejected
                                                   * why verification passed or failed
                                                   * what policies were applied
                                                   * what bundle fields influenced the decision
If the UI cannot explain it, the architecture is already drifting.
________________


The deepest form of the risk
At the deepest level, the real risk is this:
You build AASL as the formal constitution of the system, but the implementation gradually creates an unwritten common law outside the constitution.
That unwritten law lives in:
                                                   * prompts
                                                   * heuristics
                                                   * service code
                                                   * manual exceptions
                                                   * hidden scores
                                                   * undocumented fields
Once that happens, the formal language stops being sovereign.
That is the real failure mode.
________________


Bottom line
The biggest hidden architectural risk is not scale, not agent count, not latency, and not even verification cost.
It is:
allowing semantically meaningful behavior to exist outside the formal AASL-governed system
That is what silently destroys architectures like this.
The safest next move is to define a Semantic Closure Policy for Atrahasis: a formal implementation rule that states exactly what kinds of meaning are allowed to exist outside AASL, and what must be modeled explicitly.
